user
You are performing an implementation-readiness review of the following Markdown specification.

Scope: this is a DOCUMENT review, not a code review. Your job is to find issues in the spec that would trip implementers or that indicate the spec's internal state is inconsistent. Point at section headings and line numbers when possible.

Context you should treat as ground truth for framing:

- The codebase is PRE-PRODUCTION. No live users. No staged rollouts. No feature flags for new migrations.
- Testing posture: static gates primary, runtime tests pure-function only. No vitest / jest / playwright / supertest / frontend unit / E2E tests of the app itself.
- Rollout model: commit_and_revert. No canaries. No percentage rollouts.
- Prefer existing primitives over new abstractions.
- Do NOT propose feature flags, staged rollouts, canary deploys, kill switches, per-tenant rollout, frontend tests, composition tests, API contract tests, E2E tests, performance baselines, or monitoring beyond what the spec already has. Those are directional changes that belong to the product owner, not the review.

This is ITERATION 4 of the review. Iterations 1, 2, and 3 have already been applied. Specifically resolved:

- Iteration 1 (resolved): 4-adapter parity, 4th direct-adapter site in skillAnalyzerService.ts:2063, analyzer row on By Source Type (5 rows), mechanical fixes C2-C15, R1-R2.
- Iteration 2 (mechanical, resolved): four-provider references in §1.2 A1 / §3.1 point 2 / §4.2 / §8 TOC / §8.5 / §16.1; analyzer sourceId = skill_analyzer_jobs.id; overhead-row per-tab matrix + OverheadRow contract §19.4; DailyTrendRow contract §19.5a; mockup tab-status string; system-callers enumeration + P1 margin-multiplier note + P4 readiness reframing.
- Iteration 2 (HITL, resolved): Top calls renamed from "by revenue" to "by cost" (keeps non-billable rows; ORDER BY cost_raw DESC; mockup header + subhead updated; TopCallRow.revenueCents nullable with a second overhead-row example); §11.4.1 "Controls implemented in P4" added; §17 deferred entry for real footer-link destinations.
- Iteration 3 (mechanical, resolved): P2 gate whitelist reconciled (both analyzer files); §11.3 endpoint-table payload types named; §19.5a DailyTrendRow.profitCents removed (derived client-side); §19.6 CallDetail extended with organisationId + subaccountId + link-target nullability; §19.5 split into §19.5.1 SubacctRow / §19.5.2 SourceTypeRow / §19.5.3 ProviderModelRow; prototype KPI card Gross Profit margin 25.6% -> 20.6% (matches §19.3 contract); §14.2 stale TASK_TYPES line removed; §12.4 extracted named pure helper `computeArchiveCutoff(retentionMonths, now)`.
- Iteration 3 (HITL, resolved - scope narrowing): `caller_cancel` verification in §10.5 and §16.3 narrowed to `caller_timeout` only (the analyzer pg-boss job has no UI-cancel surface today); §8.1 reworded so it no longer claims the analyzer migration wires user-cancel; new §17 Deferred entry added for "User-initiated cancel wiring for analyzer LLM calls (`caller_cancel`)". Schema-level `abort_reason = 'caller_cancel'` stays in the CHECK constraint so no future migration is needed.

Focus this iteration on any NEW issues those changes may have introduced, and on anything iterations 1-3 missed. Particular areas to scan hard:

- §8.1 now says the analyzer migration wires the `caller_timeout` path only, with user-cancel deferred to §17. Cross-check: does any other section of the spec still imply the analyzer wires user-cancel? (§5, §8.2-§8.5, §10.1, §11.6, §19.6 CallDetail, §19.8 CallDetail example, §19.9 envelope examples, prototype Top calls sample rows.)
- The new §17 entry for user-cancel wiring — does it read cleanly against §8.1 (which now points at §17) and §10.5 (which no longer tests user-cancel)?
- §17 now has 9 deferred entries. Are they all non-overlapping and each backed by a concrete reason?
- §19.5 split from one table into three contracts §19.5.1/.2/.3 in iter-3 — do §11.2 service docstrings and §11.3 endpoint table point at the right sub-section names? Any dangling reference to "§19.5" that should now be more specific?
- §19.5a DailyTrendRow lost `profitCents` in iter-3 — is every consumer in §11 (KPI deltas + chart line) now deriving net profit client-side? Any prose that still says the endpoint returns profit?
- §19.6 CallDetail gained `organisationId` + `subaccountId` — does the §11.6 drawer spec reflect the new fields, and does the §11.3 `/top-calls/:id` endpoint documentation mention them?
- §12.4 `computeArchiveCutoff(retentionMonths, now)` — does §14.5 Files and §14.8a Files agree on the new `llmLedgerArchiveJobPure.ts` file? Is the pure helper import path consistent?
- Prototype at `prototypes/system-costs-page.html`: post iter-3 margin fix (25.6% -> 20.6%), are all other KPI numbers still internally consistent with §19.3? Do the prototype's "Top calls" sample rows match the now-cost-ordered ordering with at least one overhead-row example?

What to look for in general:

1. CONTRADICTIONS - the same concept described two different ways in different sections.
2. STALE / RETIRED LANGUAGE - approaches the spec explicitly rejected still appearing in prose.
3. LOAD-BEARING CLAIMS WITHOUT CONTRACTS - "X must be idempotent" without a mechanism named.
4. FILE-INVENTORY DRIFT - prose mentions a file/column/migration that is not in the §14 Files table (or vice versa).
5. SCHEMA OVERLAPS - two columns or tables with adjacent purposes without a source-of-truth statement.
6. SEQUENCING BUGS - Phase N depends on something created in Phase N+k.
7. INVARIANTS stated in one section but not enforced in another.
8. MISSING PER-PHASE VERDICTS - items without an explicit phase assignment.
9. UNNAMED new primitives - "a new service that does X" without naming the file/function/type.
10. MISSING CONTRACTS - a data shape crossing a service boundary with no §19 Contracts entry.
11. PATH REFERENCES that don't match the actual repo layout.
12. CHECK-constraint / invariant WEAKNESSES - does the CHECK in §6.1 enforce what §5.1 prose claims?
13. DEFERRED ITEMS drift - is every "deferred" / "later" / "future" reference in prose listed in §17?

Output format: a numbered list of findings. For each finding, include:
- A short label
- The section(s) affected
- A one-to-three sentence description of the issue
- Your suggested fix (concrete, implementable - not "consider reviewing")
- Severity: critical / important / minor / nit

Be direct. Do not hedge. Do not pad. If you see no issue in a given area, say nothing about it. If the spec is clean in a given area, do not mention it.

The spec file is at `tasks/llm-observability-ledger-generalisation-spec.md` in the current workdir. Also review `prototypes/system-costs-page.html` which is part of the spec surface (§11 calls it the authoritative UI mockup). Read both files fully before producing your findings.

86:
87:- **Contracts** are called out explicitly per §3 of `docs/spec-authoring-checklist.md`. Every data shape crossing a service boundary has a Contracts entry in §19.
88:- **Migration numbers** use the next free sequence from `migrations/` as of 2026-04-20 (latest is 0179 — this spec claims 0180, 0181, 0182, and 0183 across phases, see §15; a prior draft reserved 0184 for a pg-boss cron registration but that was cut because job registration is application code, not DDL).
89:- **Phase labels** are P1–P5 and map 1:1 to the sequencing graph in §15.
90:- **Reference UI** — the authoritative visual reference for §11 is `prototypes/system-costs-page.html` (committed to this branch), which includes all four tab views with worked dummy data.
91:
92:---
93:
94:*Section content begins below.*
95:
96:---
97:
98:## 1. Executive summary & outcome
99:
100:### 1.1 What this spec delivers
101:
102:Four coordinated changes to turn the existing `llm_requests` ledger from an agent-centric audit trail into a **universal, P&L-grade record of every LLM call the platform makes**, no matter which consumer initiated it:
103:
104:1. **Generalise the ledger's attribution model** so non-agent consumers (skill analyzer, workspace-memory compile, belief extraction, future background jobs) plug in with zero new FK columns per consumer. Polymorphic `sourceId` + extended `sourceType` enum + freeform `featureTag` column. See §5.1, §5.2, §6.
105:2. **Harden the adapter layer** with an `AbortController`, explicit HTTP 499 detection, and a truncated parse-failure response excerpt. These close the three observability gaps that made the skill-analyzer incident that kicked off this spec impossible to diagnose from our own data. See §8.
106:3. **Migrate the skill analyzer** off direct `anthropicAdapter.call()` and onto `llmRouter.routeCall()` as the proof-of-concept consumer. After this lands, analyzer calls show up in `llm_requests`, `cost_aggregates`, the Usage page, and the new System P&L page — every future direct-adapter caller becomes a review gate, not the default. See §10.
107:4. **Ship a System P&L admin page** at `/system/llm-pnl` that surfaces platform-wide revenue, cost, gross profit, platform overhead, and net profit across four grouping axes (organisation / subaccount / source type / provider & model). First client-side surface for cross-org financials; UI anchor is `prototypes/system-costs-page.html`. See §11.
108:
109:### 1.2 The outcome, stated as verifiable assertions
110:
111:Per `CLAUDE.md §1` — rewriting goals as verifiable assertions:
112:
113:- **A1 — No dark LLM calls.** `scripts/gates/verify-no-direct-adapter-calls.sh` fails CI when any non-test file outside `server/services/llmRouter.ts` and `server/services/providers/*.ts` imports any registered provider adapter directly (`anthropicAdapter`, `openaiAdapter`, `geminiAdapter`, `openrouterAdapter`, and any adapter added to `server/services/providers/registry.ts` in the future). The only exceptions in the final tree are test files and the router itself.
114:- **A2 — Analyzer spend is attributable.** After the analyzer migration lands, a SQL query against `llm_requests` filtered by `featureTag = 'skill-analyzer-classify'` returns rows whose `providerRequestId` matches what the Anthropic console shows for the same time window.
115:- **A3 — 499s are first-class.** A classify call that is aborted by our side produces a row with `status = 'aborted_by_caller'` (and the rarer provider-side `client_disconnected` is its own distinct status — see §6.4 for the exact mapping). Verified by manual check per §16.3 on P3 merge: kill a classify mid-flight and confirm the written row's status.
116:- **A4 — Parse failures are debuggable from our own data.** When the LLM returns unparseable JSON, the row carries a non-null `parseFailureRawExcerpt` capped at 2 KB. Verified by the pure-function test on the UTF-8 truncation helper (§14.8a) and the manual check per §16.3 on P3 merge.
117:- **A5 — System costs are visible.** A platform admin visiting `/system/llm-pnl` sees a dedicated "Platform overhead" row in every tab view, showing total system spend, no revenue attribution, and correctly subtracted from Gross profit to produce Net profit.
118:- **A6 — `cost_aggregates` supports the new dimension.** Querying aggregates by `entity_type = 'source_type'` returns per-source-type rollups for any given period, populated by the same `llm-aggregate-update` job that feeds existing dimensions.
119:- **A7 — Retention is bounded.** A nightly pg-boss job moves `llm_requests` rows older than N months into `llm_requests_archive`. N is configurable via `env.LLM_LEDGER_RETENTION_MONTHS` (default: 12). `cost_aggregates` rollups stay forever.
120:
121:### 1.3 Why this is one spec, not several
122:
123:Each of the four changes above is individually small. Taken separately, each one tempts the author to "just wire it in and skip the plumbing" — which is exactly how the analyzer ended up bypassing the router in the first place. The coordinated change is:
124:
125:> Make the ledger generic enough that the next new consumer has **no architectural choice** but to route through it.
126:
127:Splitting this into separate specs risks landing (1) without (2) and leaving parse failures still invisible, or landing (3) without (1) and adding `analyzerJobId` as an FK column (the debt outcome described in §5.1). The pieces co-constrain each other. One spec, phased rollout (§15).
128:
129:---
130:
131:## 2. Problem statement — why the status quo fails
132:
133:### 2.1 The incident that produced this spec
134:
135:On 2026-04-20 the skill-analyzer ran a 37-skill import against a marketing-heavy skill library. The UI showed "Classifying with AI..." at 60% for over 4 minutes with visible slowness. When the session tried to diagnose it:
136:
137:- **No server-side log file existed** — `logger.ts` at [server/lib/logger.ts](server/lib/logger.ts) is JSON-to-stdout only. Logs went to whatever terminal ran `npm run dev` and were lost when that terminal closed.
138:- **No entries in `llm_requests`** — the analyzer bypasses `llmRouter` entirely and calls `anthropicAdapter.call()` directly at three sites in [server/jobs/skillAnalyzerJob.ts](server/jobs/skillAnalyzerJob.ts) (lines 768, 1321, 1459).
139:- **No entries in `cost_aggregates`** — derivative of the above.
140:- **The only source of truth was the Anthropic console**, which showed two `client_error: true, code: 499, "Client disconnected"` events at latencies of 15.5s and 73.8s with token outputs of 4819 and 1197 — mid-generation aborts, not timeouts.
141:- **Our side had no record** that those disconnects even happened, let alone why.
142:
143:The incident exposed three dimensions of the same root cause: **direct-adapter calls are a dark code path**. Cost, attribution, latency, failure mode, token usage, provider request IDs — none of it exists for the analyzer.
144:
145:### 2.2 Architectural root cause
146:
147:The existing `llm_requests` table is *well-designed but consumer-specific*. Its attribution columns hard-code the three original consumers of the router (`agentRuns`, `executions`, `ieeRuns`) via typed FKs:
148:
149:```ts
150:// server/db/schema/llmRequests.ts:29-35
151:runId:       uuid('run_id').references(() => agentRuns.id),
152:executionId: uuid('execution_id').references(() => executions.id),
153:ieeRunId:    uuid('iee_run_id').references(() => ieeRuns.id),
154:```
155:
156:A fourth consumer (analyzer) has three structural options, and the rational one has not yet been taken:
157:
158:1. Leave all three FKs null and lose SQL-level linkage back to the analyzer job. **Debt.**
159:2. Add a `analyzerJobId` column to the ledger. Every next consumer adds a column. **Debt that compounds.**
160:3. Migrate to a polymorphic `sourceId uuid + sourceType text` pattern alongside the existing typed FKs. **The correct move; this spec proposes it.**
161:
162:The router itself (`llmRouter.routeCall`) is already substantially generic — its signature doesn't require agent-specific concepts. The narrow-widening work is in the ledger schema, not in the router signature. See §5.1 and §7 for details.
163:
164:### 2.3 Three gaps that made the incident undebuggable
165:
166:Each is a small but load-bearing gap in the current ledger contract:
167:
168:| Gap | What broke | Fix location | Section |
169:|---|---|---|---|
170:| No HTTP 499 discrimination | `client_disconnected` collapses into `error` — can't tell "our side hung up mid-response" from "model returned an error" | `status` enum in `llm_requests` + mapping in adapter | §6.4, §8.2 |
171:| No raw-response excerpt on parse failures | When Sonnet returns unparseable JSON we log to stdout once then lose it | New `parseFailureRawExcerpt` nullable column (≤2 KB) | §6.4, §8.3 |
172:| No clean cancellation primitive in the adapter | `Promise.race` abandons the fetch, socket RSTs eventually — shows as an unexplained 499 on Anthropic's side | `AbortController` threaded through `ProviderCallParams` | §8.1 |
173:
174:### 2.4 Product-level problem — zero cross-org financial visibility
175:
176:Separate from the observability gap: today there is **no UI surface where a platform operator can see LLM spend across multiple organisations at once**. The endpoint `/api/admin/usage/overview` exists at [server/routes/llmUsage.ts:479](server/routes/llmUsage.ts) but has no client caller. There is no `SystemUsagePage`, no `/system/costs` route, no `/system/llm-pnl` route.
177:
178:This matters more than "operator convenience" because:
179:
180:- **Revenue attribution requires cross-org rollup.** You cannot see whether the platform is making money without aggregating `costWithMargin` across every org in one view.
181:- **System-level spend has no home today.** Rows with `sourceType='system'` already exist in the ledger (written today by `workspaceMemoryService`, `agentBriefingService`, `skillEmbeddingService`, `outcomeLearningService`, and `skillExecutor` — see `rg "sourceType.*'system'" server/`), but there is no admin surface that aggregates them. P3 adds `sourceType='analyzer'` as a sibling taxonomy so the analyzer's non-trivial spend stops being pooled into "system." Adding the System P&L page at the same time is what makes both taxonomies *useful* rather than just *stored*.
182:
183:### 2.5 Why this is urgent (not just nice-to-have)
184:
185:- The analyzer today writes nothing to `llm_requests`. Every analyzer run silently burns provider budget with no ledger row, no cost-aggregate row, no billing attribution. The longer this persists, the more drift accumulates between "what we paid providers" and "what the ledger says we paid providers."
186:- Other direct-adapter callers may exist and are un-audited. §9 covers the sweep — there is a non-zero probability that production-path code other than the analyzer is also dark. We don't know until we look.
187:- The `System P&L` page is the single most-requested platform-operator view. Until it exists, the CEO cannot answer "is this business making money this month?" from inside the product.
188:
189:---
190:
191:## 3. Goals & non-goals
192:
193:### 3.1 In-scope goals
194:
195:1. **Generalise `llm_requests` attribution** so any current or future consumer (agent run, process execution, IEE run, analyzer job, future background job, admin tool) produces ledger rows without a schema change per consumer.
196:2. **Close the three adapter-level observability gaps** (499 discrimination, parse-failure excerpt, AbortController) uniformly across every registered provider adapter (`anthropicAdapter`, `openaiAdapter`, `geminiAdapter`, `openrouterAdapter`) — see §8.4 for parity matrix.
197:3. **Migrate the skill-analyzer** to route through `llmRouter` end-to-end, retiring all three direct `anthropicAdapter.call()` sites in `skillAnalyzerJob.ts`.
198:4. **Extend `cost_aggregates`** with a `sourceType` dimension so system-level spend can be rolled up and displayed separately from org-billable spend.
199:5. **Ship a System P&L admin page** at `/system/llm-pnl` with four grouping tabs (organisation / subaccount / source type / provider-model), four KPI cards (Revenue / Gross profit / Platform overhead / Net profit), a 30-day trend chart, and a top-calls-by-cost list (ranked by cost desc, includes platform-overhead rows). UI contract: `prototypes/system-costs-page.html`.
200:6. **Add a nightly retention job** that moves `llm_requests` rows older than `env.LLM_LEDGER_RETENTION_MONTHS` (default 12) into a `llm_requests_archive` table of identical shape, with lighter indexing.
201:7. **Enforce no-regression** via a new static gate `scripts/gates/verify-no-direct-adapter-calls.sh` that fails CI if any non-router, non-test file imports the adapters directly.
202:8. **Audit the codebase** for other direct-adapter callers (§9) and produce a remediation plan — not necessarily remediation itself within this spec.
203:
204:### 3.2 Out of scope (explicitly non-goals)
205:
206:These were considered and rejected for this spec — they are not deferred, they are **not in scope and should not be added**:
207:
208:- **Replacing the router.** The router is fit for purpose; this spec extends its context shape, not its responsibilities.
209:- **Replacing `agentExecutionService`'s existing attribution path.** Agent runs already write to `llm_requests` via the router correctly. This spec's polymorphic pattern is *additive* — typed FKs (`runId`, `executionId`, `ieeRunId`) remain and continue to be the primary attribution mechanism for their consumers. New consumers use the polymorphic columns.
210:- **Per-call streaming of responses.** Anthropic non-streaming is fine for the analyzer's use case; streaming support is a separate spec.
211:- **A cost-forecasting or budget-prediction layer.** `docs/spec-context.md` convention_rejections explicitly excludes "predictive cost modelling or tool success scoring loops."
212:- **E2E tests against the P&L page.** `frontend_tests: none_for_now` per framing.
213:- **A database-backed application log table.** Option 2 from the earlier conversation (file transport for `logger.ts`) is a useful but separate concern; this spec does not require it. Once `llm_requests` captures every call, stdout-only `logger.ts` is acceptable for the residual non-LLM events.
214:- **A billing invoice workflow.** Revenue on the P&L page is `costWithMargin` from the ledger, not a billing artefact. Invoices are a downstream concern.
215:- **MCP tool call observability.** MCP tool calls that invoke an LLM do so through the same adapters and will inherit this observability; MCP tool calls that don't invoke an LLM (pure IO) are out of scope.
216:
217:### 3.3 Non-goals that are genuinely deferred (see §17)
218:
219:These are in the Deferred Items section with explicit phase pointers:
220:
221:- Detail drawer rich-state interactions (tooltip, filter by request ID, "copy as support ticket")
222:- Auto-archival of matched `cost_aggregates` rows older than 24 months
223:- Provider-level cost reconciliation (comparing our cost to Anthropic invoice dumps)
224:- Anomaly alerting on System P&L metrics (e.g. "Platform overhead >15% of revenue for 3 consecutive days")
225:
226:---
227:
228:## 4. Existing primitives audit
229:
230:Per §1 of `docs/spec-authoring-checklist.md`, every new primitive this spec introduces carries a "why not reuse" paragraph. This section walks through each candidate primitive and states the decision.
231:
232:### 4.1 Tables
233:
234:| Proposing | Status | Rationale |
235:|---|---|---|
236:| New LLM log table (`llm_logs` in the earlier rejected draft) | **REJECTED — reuse** `llm_requests` | The earlier draft of this spec (noted in conversation history) proposed `llm_logs`. Audit showed `llm_requests` already captures 100% of the columns the new table would carry, plus 30+ more. Building a parallel table was the wrong answer. Spec pivoted to extending `llm_requests`. |
237:| New attribution table (e.g. `llm_request_sources`) | **REJECTED — extend existing** | An attribution junction table would require an extra JOIN on every query. The polymorphic `sourceId` + `sourceType` pattern on `llm_requests` is a one-column change that serves the same purpose. See §5.1 rejected alternatives. |
238:| `llm_requests_archive` | **NEW PRIMITIVE** | No existing archival pattern for financial-audit rows. Why not reuse: `cost_aggregates` is a rollup, not an archive — it loses per-call detail. Why not defer: unbounded growth on `llm_requests` is operational debt that gets worse with time. Why new: keeps the same shape as the live table so queries work identically after joining, with lighter indexing to reduce write amplification. |
239:
240:### 4.2 Services
241:
242:| Proposing | Status | Rationale |
243:|---|---|---|
244:| `llmRouter.routeCall()` extensions | **EXTEND** | New fields on `LLMCallContextSchema`, two new system-caller policy branches. Router responsibility doesn't change. |
245:| `costAggregateService.upsertAggregates()` — `sourceType` dimension | **EXTEND** | Add one more entity type to the existing dimension enum. Same service, same job, same upsert key shape. |
246:| Adapter layer (every adapter in `server/services/providers/registry.ts` — `anthropicAdapter`, `openaiAdapter`, `geminiAdapter`, `openrouterAdapter`) | **EXTEND** | New `signal` param, new error mapping, new parse-failure capture. Adapter contract grows but stays adapter-shaped. Uniform across every registered provider per §8.4. |
247:| `systemPnlService` (new) | **NEW PRIMITIVE** | No existing service cross-aggregates across organisations. `llmUsageService` is org-scoped (every method filters by `organisationId`). Why not reuse: making `llmUsageService` dual-purpose (org-scoped and platform-scoped) blurs the scoping boundary the RLS guard relies on. A separate system service with its own principal-scoping check is clearer and safer. |
248:| `systemAdminLedgerService` or similar | **REJECTED — inline in `systemPnlService`** | One service is enough; no need to split. |
249:

11:## Framing statements (spec-context concurrence)
12:
13:This spec is authored against `docs/spec-context.md` as of 2026-04-16. The following framing applies — any deviation is flagged inline:
14:
15:- `pre_production: yes` — rollout is `commit_and_revert`, no staged percentage rollouts, no feature flags for new migrations.
16:- `testing_posture: static_gates_primary` + `runtime_tests: pure_function_only` — no vitest / jest / supertest / frontend unit / E2E tests proposed.
17:- `prefer_existing_primitives_over_new_ones: yes` — every new primitive this spec proposes carries a "why not reuse" paragraph.
18:- `breaking_changes_expected: yes` — adapter signatures and router contract may grow; no backward-compat shims.
19:
20:Override: none. If reviewer flags a directional finding against these defaults, treat it as a framing check — this spec does not override them.

138:- **No entries in `llm_requests`** — the analyzer bypasses `llmRouter` entirely and calls `anthropicAdapter.call()` directly at three sites in [server/jobs/skillAnalyzerJob.ts](server/jobs/skillAnalyzerJob.ts) (lines 768, 1321, 1459).
139:- **No entries in `cost_aggregates`** — derivative of the above.
140:- **The only source of truth was the Anthropic console**, which showed two `client_error: true, code: 499, "Client disconnected"` events at latencies of 15.5s and 73.8s with token outputs of 4819 and 1197 — mid-generation aborts, not timeouts.
141:- **Our side had no record** that those disconnects even happened, let alone why.
142:
143:The incident exposed three dimensions of the same root cause: **direct-adapter calls are a dark code path**. Cost, attribution, latency, failure mode, token usage, provider request IDs — none of it exists for the analyzer.
144:
145:### 2.2 Architectural root cause
146:
147:The existing `llm_requests` table is *well-designed but consumer-specific*. Its attribution columns hard-code the three original consumers of the router (`agentRuns`, `executions`, `ieeRuns`) via typed FKs:
148:
149:```ts
150:// server/db/schema/llmRequests.ts:29-35
151:runId:       uuid('run_id').references(() => agentRuns.id),
152:executionId: uuid('execution_id').references(() => executions.id),
153:ieeRunId:    uuid('iee_run_id').references(() => ieeRuns.id),
154:```
155:
156:A fourth consumer (analyzer) has three structural options, and the rational one has not yet been taken:
157:
158:1. Leave all three FKs null and lose SQL-level linkage back to the analyzer job. **Debt.**
159:2. Add a `analyzerJobId` column to the ledger. Every next consumer adds a column. **Debt that compounds.**
160:3. Migrate to a polymorphic `sourceId uuid + sourceType text` pattern alongside the existing typed FKs. **The correct move; this spec proposes it.**
161:
162:The router itself (`llmRouter.routeCall`) is already substantially generic — its signature doesn't require agent-specific concepts. The narrow-widening work is in the ledger schema, not in the router signature. See §5.1 and §7 for details.
163:
164:### 2.3 Three gaps that made the incident undebuggable
165:
166:Each is a small but load-bearing gap in the current ledger contract:
167:
168:| Gap | What broke | Fix location | Section |
169:|---|---|---|---|
170:| No HTTP 499 discrimination | `client_disconnected` collapses into `error` — can't tell "our side hung up mid-response" from "model returned an error" | `status` enum in `llm_requests` + mapping in adapter | §6.4, §8.2 |
171:| No raw-response excerpt on parse failures | When Sonnet returns unparseable JSON we log to stdout once then lose it | New `parseFailureRawExcerpt` nullable column (≤2 KB) | §6.4, §8.3 |
172:| No clean cancellation primitive in the adapter | `Promise.race` abandons the fetch, socket RSTs eventually — shows as an unexplained 499 on Anthropic's side | `AbortController` threaded through `ProviderCallParams` | §8.1 |
173:
174:### 2.4 Product-level problem — zero cross-org financial visibility
175:
176:Separate from the observability gap: today there is **no UI surface where a platform operator can see LLM spend across multiple organisations at once**. The endpoint `/api/admin/usage/overview` exists at [server/routes/llmUsage.ts:479](server/routes/llmUsage.ts) but has no client caller. There is no `SystemUsagePage`, no `/system/costs` route, no `/system/llm-pnl` route.
177:
178:This matters more than "operator convenience" because:
179:
180:- **Revenue attribution requires cross-org rollup.** You cannot see whether the platform is making money without aggregating `costWithMargin` across every org in one view.
181:- **System-level spend has no home today.** Rows with `sourceType='system'` already exist in the ledger (written today by `workspaceMemoryService`, `agentBriefingService`, `skillEmbeddingService`, `outcomeLearningService`, and `skillExecutor` — see `rg "sourceType.*'system'" server/`), but there is no admin surface that aggregates them. P3 adds `sourceType='analyzer'` as a sibling taxonomy so the analyzer's non-trivial spend stops being pooled into "system." Adding the System P&L page at the same time is what makes both taxonomies *useful* rather than just *stored*.
182:
183:### 2.5 Why this is urgent (not just nice-to-have)
184:
185:- The analyzer today writes nothing to `llm_requests`. Every analyzer run silently burns provider budget with no ledger row, no cost-aggregate row, no billing attribution. The longer this persists, the more drift accumulates between "what we paid providers" and "what the ledger says we paid providers."
186:- Other direct-adapter callers may exist and are un-audited. §9 covers the sweep — there is a non-zero probability that production-path code other than the analyzer is also dark. We don't know until we look.
187:- The `System P&L` page is the single most-requested platform-operator view. Until it exists, the CEO cannot answer "is this business making money this month?" from inside the product.
188:
189:---
190:
191:## 3. Goals & non-goals
192:
193:### 3.1 In-scope goals
194:
195:1. **Generalise `llm_requests` attribution** so any current or future consumer (agent run, process execution, IEE run, analyzer job, future background job, admin tool) produces ledger rows without a schema change per consumer.
196:2. **Close the three adapter-level observability gaps** (499 discrimination, parse-failure excerpt, AbortController) uniformly across every registered provider adapter (`anthropicAdapter`, `openaiAdapter`, `geminiAdapter`, `openrouterAdapter`) — see §8.4 for parity matrix.
197:3. **Migrate the skill-analyzer** to route through `llmRouter` end-to-end, retiring all three direct `anthropicAdapter.call()` sites in `skillAnalyzerJob.ts`.
198:4. **Extend `cost_aggregates`** with a `sourceType` dimension so system-level spend can be rolled up and displayed separately from org-billable spend.
199:5. **Ship a System P&L admin page** at `/system/llm-pnl` with four grouping tabs (organisation / subaccount / source type / provider-model), four KPI cards (Revenue / Gross profit / Platform overhead / Net profit), a 30-day trend chart, and a top-calls-by-cost list (ranked by cost desc, includes platform-overhead rows). UI contract: `prototypes/system-costs-page.html`.
200:6. **Add a nightly retention job** that moves `llm_requests` rows older than `env.LLM_LEDGER_RETENTION_MONTHS` (default 12) into a `llm_requests_archive` table of identical shape, with lighter indexing.
201:7. **Enforce no-regression** via a new static gate `scripts/gates/verify-no-direct-adapter-calls.sh` that fails CI if any non-router, non-test file imports the adapters directly.
202:8. **Audit the codebase** for other direct-adapter callers (§9) and produce a remediation plan — not necessarily remediation itself within this spec.
203:
204:### 3.2 Out of scope (explicitly non-goals)
205:
206:These were considered and rejected for this spec — they are not deferred, they are **not in scope and should not be added**:
207:
208:- **Replacing the router.** The router is fit for purpose; this spec extends its context shape, not its responsibilities.
209:- **Replacing `agentExecutionService`'s existing attribution path.** Agent runs already write to `llm_requests` via the router correctly. This spec's polymorphic pattern is *additive* — typed FKs (`runId`, `executionId`, `ieeRunId`) remain and continue to be the primary attribution mechanism for their consumers. New consumers use the polymorphic columns.
210:- **Per-call streaming of responses.** Anthropic non-streaming is fine for the analyzer's use case; streaming support is a separate spec.
211:- **A cost-forecasting or budget-prediction layer.** `docs/spec-context.md` convention_rejections explicitly excludes "predictive cost modelling or tool success scoring loops."
212:- **E2E tests against the P&L page.** `frontend_tests: none_for_now` per framing.
213:- **A database-backed application log table.** Option 2 from the earlier conversation (file transport for `logger.ts`) is a useful but separate concern; this spec does not require it. Once `llm_requests` captures every call, stdout-only `logger.ts` is acceptable for the residual non-LLM events.
214:- **A billing invoice workflow.** Revenue on the P&L page is `costWithMargin` from the ledger, not a billing artefact. Invoices are a downstream concern.
215:- **MCP tool call observability.** MCP tool calls that invoke an LLM do so through the same adapters and will inherit this observability; MCP tool calls that don't invoke an LLM (pure IO) are out of scope.
216:
217:### 3.3 Non-goals that are genuinely deferred (see §17)
218:
219:These are in the Deferred Items section with explicit phase pointers:
220:
221:- Detail drawer rich-state interactions (tooltip, filter by request ID, "copy as support ticket")
222:- Auto-archival of matched `cost_aggregates` rows older than 24 months
223:- Provider-level cost reconciliation (comparing our cost to Anthropic invoice dumps)
224:- Anomaly alerting on System P&L metrics (e.g. "Platform overhead >15% of revenue for 3 consecutive days")
225:
226:---
227:
228:## 4. Existing primitives audit
229:
230:Per §1 of `docs/spec-authoring-checklist.md`, every new primitive this spec introduces carries a "why not reuse" paragraph. This section walks through each candidate primitive and states the decision.
231:
232:### 4.1 Tables
233:
234:| Proposing | Status | Rationale |
235:|---|---|---|
236:| New LLM log table (`llm_logs` in the earlier rejected draft) | **REJECTED — reuse** `llm_requests` | The earlier draft of this spec (noted in conversation history) proposed `llm_logs`. Audit showed `llm_requests` already captures 100% of the columns the new table would carry, plus 30+ more. Building a parallel table was the wrong answer. Spec pivoted to extending `llm_requests`. |
237:| New attribution table (e.g. `llm_request_sources`) | **REJECTED — extend existing** | An attribution junction table would require an extra JOIN on every query. The polymorphic `sourceId` + `sourceType` pattern on `llm_requests` is a one-column change that serves the same purpose. See §5.1 rejected alternatives. |
238:| `llm_requests_archive` | **NEW PRIMITIVE** | No existing archival pattern for financial-audit rows. Why not reuse: `cost_aggregates` is a rollup, not an archive — it loses per-call detail. Why not defer: unbounded growth on `llm_requests` is operational debt that gets worse with time. Why new: keeps the same shape as the live table so queries work identically after joining, with lighter indexing to reduce write amplification. |
239:
240:### 4.2 Services
241:
242:| Proposing | Status | Rationale |
243:|---|---|---|
244:| `llmRouter.routeCall()` extensions | **EXTEND** | New fields on `LLMCallContextSchema`, two new system-caller policy branches. Router responsibility doesn't change. |
245:| `costAggregateService.upsertAggregates()` — `sourceType` dimension | **EXTEND** | Add one more entity type to the existing dimension enum. Same service, same job, same upsert key shape. |
246:| Adapter layer (every adapter in `server/services/providers/registry.ts` — `anthropicAdapter`, `openaiAdapter`, `geminiAdapter`, `openrouterAdapter`) | **EXTEND** | New `signal` param, new error mapping, new parse-failure capture. Adapter contract grows but stays adapter-shaped. Uniform across every registered provider per §8.4. |
247:| `systemPnlService` (new) | **NEW PRIMITIVE** | No existing service cross-aggregates across organisations. `llmUsageService` is org-scoped (every method filters by `organisationId`). Why not reuse: making `llmUsageService` dual-purpose (org-scoped and platform-scoped) blurs the scoping boundary the RLS guard relies on. A separate system service with its own principal-scoping check is clearer and safer. |
248:| `systemAdminLedgerService` or similar | **REJECTED — inline in `systemPnlService`** | One service is enough; no need to split. |
249:
250:### 4.3 Routes

2026-04-20T06:51:09.045920Z ERROR codex_core::tools::router: error=Exit code: 1
Wall time: 0.4 seconds
Output:
251:
252:| Proposing | Status | Rationale |
253:|---|---|---|
254:| `/api/admin/usage/overview` existing route | **NO CHANGE — left in place** | Route already requires `requireSystemAdmin` and serves the existing subaccount-scoped Usage page. The P&L page's new grouping shapes are shaped differently enough (platform-admin cross-org, different cache profile, different response envelope) that a new router is cleaner than grafting onto the existing endpoint. See §11.3 and §14.4. |
255:| `/api/admin/llm-pnl/*` (new routes) | **NEW** | New aggregated endpoints for the 4-tab grouping, the 30-day trend, and the top-calls-by-cost list. Why not reuse: fits badly inside the existing overview endpoint (response shape mismatch, different cache profile). |
256:| `/api/admin/llm-calls/:id` (call detail) | **NEW** | No existing per-call detail endpoint. System-admin-only; read from `llm_requests` directly (no RLS bypass — admin is explicitly cross-tenant). |

293:
294:## 5. Design decisions — the four fault lines
295:
296:Each subsection below names a directional design decision, the decision taken, and the rejected alternatives (with reasons). These are the questions the `spec-reviewer` agent will pause for HITL on if they are implicit — pinning them here prevents that.
297:
298:### 5.1 Attribution pattern — polymorphic `sourceId` vs FK-per-consumer
299:
300:**Decision:** Introduce two new columns on `llm_requests`:
301:
302:- `sourceId uuid` — polymorphic pointer. When populated, points to a row in whichever table `sourceType` names. No referential integrity constraint (FK would have to be to multiple tables).
303:- `sourceType` remains the existing `text` column, but is extended with additional values (see §5.2's adjacent decision).
304:
305:Existing typed FKs (`runId`, `executionId`, `ieeRunId`) are **kept as-is**. They are the primary attribution mechanism for their respective consumers — the polymorphic pattern is *additive*, used only by new consumers who don't have a typed FK.
306:
307:**Assertion that makes this unambiguous:** For any row in `llm_requests`, exactly one of the following holds:
308:
309:- `sourceType = 'agent_run'` AND `runId IS NOT NULL` AND `sourceId IS NULL`
310:- `sourceType = 'process_execution'` AND `executionId IS NOT NULL` AND `sourceId IS NULL`
311:- `sourceType = 'iee'` AND `ieeRunId IS NOT NULL` AND `sourceId IS NULL`
312:- `sourceType IN ('system', 'analyzer', …future values…)` AND `sourceId IS NOT NULL` AND all three typed FKs NULL
313:- `sourceType = 'system'` AND `sourceId IS NULL` (legacy system rows without attribution; preserved for backward compat)
314:
315:Enforced by a database `CHECK` constraint (see §6.1).
316:
317:**Rejected alternatives:**
318:
319:- **Column-per-consumer.** Adding `analyzerJobId` then `workspaceMemoryCompileJobId` then the next one. Schema grows linearly with consumer count. Every addition requires a migration and a backfill. **Rejected as compounding debt.**
320:- **Remove typed FKs, use only polymorphic.** Clean in theory; catastrophic to migrate. Existing queries, existing indexes, existing joins across `agent_runs ↔ llm_requests` would all break. The downside of keeping typed FKs (a bit of schema asymmetry) is much smaller than the cost of a deep rewrite. **Rejected on pragmatism.**
321:- **Junction table `llm_request_sources`.** Would require an extra JOIN on every ledger read. For a high-write table this is measurable. **Rejected on query-path cost.**
322:
323:**Load-bearing mechanism:** the `CHECK` constraint in migration 0180. Without it, the invariant is prose; with it, the invariant is enforced.
324:
325:### 5.2 Taxonomy pattern — `taskType` enum extension vs `featureTag` freeform
326:
327:**Decision:** Keep `taskType` as a closed enum (it already has 10 values). **Do not extend it** for new consumers. Add a new column:
328:
329:- `featureTag text NOT NULL DEFAULT 'unknown'` — freeform kebab-case identifier for the specific LLM use case. Examples: `skill-analyzer-classify`, `skill-analyzer-agent-match`, `skill-analyzer-cluster-recommend`, `workspace-memory-compile`, `belief-extraction`, `hyde-expansion`.
330:
331:Router callers must set it; default `'unknown'` exists only to make the column `NOT NULL` without breaking existing code paths that might silently not yet set it. A static check at the router level logs a warning when a call arrives with `featureTag = 'unknown'` in non-test code.
332:
333:**Why two separate columns (`taskType` + `featureTag`)?** They answer different questions:
334:
335:- `taskType` answers "what class of work is this?" — used by model routing (`resolveLLM()` consumes it).
336:- `featureTag` answers "which feature is this?" — used by cost-attribution dashboards and the System P&L page.
337:
338:A reader of the Usage page wants to see feature-level breakdowns ("how much did the analyzer cost this week?"). A router making model-selection decisions wants to see task-level classes (`general`, `qa_validation`, `memory_compile`). Conflating them into one column makes either one slightly worse at its job.
339:
340:**Rejected alternatives:**
341:
342:- **Extend `taskType` with `skill_classify` etc.** Closed enum = migration per feature = churn. Also conflates routing policy concepts with reporting concepts. **Rejected.**
343:- **Overload `agentName` as a feature tag.** `agentName` is only meaningful for agent runs; using it for non-agent callers would break its existing semantics for the Usage page's "by agent" breakdown. **Rejected.**
344:- **JSONB metadata column.** Too flexible; makes aggregation slow and reporting brittle. **Rejected.**
345:
346:### 5.3 `executionPhase` semantics for non-agent callers
347:
348:**Decision:** Make `executionPhase` nullable. The existing enum (`planning | execution | synthesis | iee_loop_step`) is agent-execution-shaped and doesn't describe "one-shot classifier call" or "background job inference." For non-agent callers:
349:
350:- `executionPhase` is **NULL** when `sourceType ∈ {'system', 'analyzer', plus any future non-agent source}`.
351:- `executionPhase` remains **required (NOT NULL)** when `sourceType ∈ {'agent_run', 'process_execution', 'iee'}`.
352:
353:Enforced by the same `CHECK` constraint as the attribution invariant (§5.1).
354:
355:**Why not add a neutral `'batch'` or `'one_shot'` enum value?** Because that value carries no useful semantics — it means "not agent execution," which is exactly what `NULL` already conveys. Adding a dummy value pollutes every dashboard that groups by phase with a meaningless bucket. NULL-as-absent is the honest representation.
356:
357:**Rejected alternatives:**
358:
359:- **Add `'batch'` value.** Dashboard clutter for zero routing benefit. **Rejected.**
360:- **Reshape `executionPhase` into a more generic `callContext` column.** Breaks every existing query. **Rejected on migration cost.**
361:
362:### 5.4 Router policy for system callers — routing resolution + budget
363:
364:**Decision:** Introduce a new enum on `LLMCallContextSchema` — `systemCallerPolicy: 'respect_routing' | 'bypass_routing'` — defaulting to `'respect_routing'`. When set to `'bypass_routing'`:
365:
366:- `resolveLLM()` is skipped; the caller's chosen `provider` and `model` are used verbatim. `capabilityTier`, `wasDowngraded`, `routingReason` remain populated for reporting (`routingReason = 'forced'`, `wasDowngraded = false`).
367:- `budgetService.checkAndReserve()` is still invoked unconditionally, but its return type is widened to `string | null` and it returns `null` (no reservation) for `sourceType ∈ {'system', 'analyzer'}`. Downstream code already tolerates `null` as "no reservation to release on error", because system calls have no billing line. See §7.2 for the exact branch and §19.10 for the updated contract.
368:
369:**Why bypass routing at all?** The analyzer has legitimate reasons to pin `claude-sonnet-4-6` for classification (the prompt is tuned for that model's JSON parse reliability). Routing would downgrade it to Haiku based on policy, breaking the spec-correctness of the analyzer's output. For migrations, this is exactly the right escape hatch — opt-in, per-call, visible in the ledger.
370:
371:**Why still go through the router (not skip entirely)?** Because the router is the only primitive that writes `llm_requests`. Bypass-routing still writes the row. Skip-router doesn't. That's the whole point of this spec.
372:
373:**Rejected alternatives:**
374:
375:- **Always route — no bypass.** Breaks analyzer correctness; analyzer Sonnet prompts are not Haiku-compatible without redesign. Also breaks any future caller that has a good reason to pin a model. **Rejected.**
376:- **Add a new `resolveLLM` strategy per caller.** Unbounded policy sprawl. **Rejected.**
377:- **Put the bypass inside the adapter.** Moves the decision to the wrong layer; the router is where routing policy belongs. **Rejected.**
378:
379:### 5.5 Summary table
380:
381:| Fault line | Decision | Mechanism | Trade-off accepted |
382:|---|---|---|---|
383:| Attribution pattern | Polymorphic `sourceId` + keep typed FKs | DB `CHECK` constraint | Schema asymmetry (acceptable) |
384:| Taxonomy pattern | New `featureTag` column, keep `taskType` enum | Static check at router call site | Two columns instead of one (intentional) |
385:| `executionPhase` for non-agents | Nullable, NULL for system/analyzer | Same `CHECK` constraint | Removes `NOT NULL` on that column |
386:| Router policy for system | `systemCallerPolicy` enum default `'respect_routing'` | New field on `LLMCallContextSchema` | Per-call opt-out (intentional) |
387:
388:---
389:
390:## 6. Data model changes
391:
392:### 6.1 `llm_requests` schema additions (migration 0180)
393:
394:Four new columns, one loosened constraint, three new `status` values, one extended `sourceType` value set, one new `CHECK` constraint.
395:
396:**Migration file:** `migrations/0180_llm_requests_generalisation.sql`
397:
398:**Column additions:**
399:
400:```sql
401:ALTER TABLE llm_requests
402:  ADD COLUMN source_id uuid,                                -- polymorphic FK (no RI)
403:  ADD COLUMN feature_tag text NOT NULL DEFAULT 'unknown',   -- kebab-case feature identifier
404:  ADD COLUMN parse_failure_raw_excerpt text,                -- ≤2 KB truncated LLM response
405:  ADD COLUMN abort_reason text;                             -- 'caller_timeout' | 'caller_cancel' | NULL
406:```
407:
408:**Constraint changes:**
409:
410:```sql
411:ALTER TABLE llm_requests ALTER COLUMN execution_phase DROP NOT NULL;
412:
413:-- Drop the `sourceType` column default so every insert path MUST specify
414:-- a source_type explicitly. The existing default `'agent_run'` would
415:-- silently satisfy a legacy NULL-runId insert and bypass the new
416:-- attribution CHECK — closing that gap is the entire point of this spec.
417:ALTER TABLE llm_requests ALTER COLUMN source_type DROP DEFAULT;
418:```
419:
420:The schema file `server/db/schema/llmRequests.ts` is updated in the same migration to remove `.default('agent_run')` from the `sourceType` column declaration. Every router insert path already sets `sourceType` explicitly today (verified during P1 — the router always has a `ctx.sourceType`), so the default is unreachable in practice. Dropping it catches the next caller who forgets.
421:
422:**Status enum extensions** (stored as free `text`; enforced by app-level enum in `llmRequests.ts`):
423:
424:- Add `'client_disconnected'` — HTTP 499 equivalent, our side aborted/closed the socket.
425:- Add `'parse_failure'` — provider returned a structurally-OK response that failed our schema check after all retries exhausted.
426:- Add `'aborted_by_caller'` — `AbortController.abort()` fired from caller code (distinct from caller_timeout).
427:
428:**sourceType enum extension** (app-level):
429:
430:- Add `'analyzer'` — skill-analyzer calls after migration.
431:- Keep `'system'` as the generic non-attributed catch-all for future system consumers that don't have their own sourceType value yet.
432:
433:**CHECK constraint — attribution invariant:**
434:
435:Every clause below fully constrains every attribution column so the invariant prose in §5.1 is encoded exactly — no attribution column can appear where it doesn't belong.
436:
437:```sql
438:ALTER TABLE llm_requests ADD CONSTRAINT llm_requests_attribution_ck CHECK (
439:  (source_type = 'agent_run'
440:     AND run_id          IS NOT NULL
441:     AND execution_id    IS NULL
442:     AND iee_run_id      IS NULL
443:     AND source_id       IS NULL)
444:  OR
445:  (source_type = 'process_execution'
446:     AND execution_id    IS NOT NULL
447:     AND run_id          IS NULL
448:     AND iee_run_id      IS NULL
449:     AND source_id       IS NULL)
450:  OR
451:  (source_type = 'iee'
452:     AND iee_run_id      IS NOT NULL
453:     AND run_id          IS NULL
454:     AND execution_id    IS NULL
455:     AND source_id       IS NULL)
456:  OR
457:  (source_type = 'analyzer'
458:     AND source_id       IS NOT NULL
459:     AND run_id          IS NULL
460:     AND execution_id    IS NULL
461:     AND iee_run_id      IS NULL)
462:  OR
463:  (source_type = 'system'
464:     AND run_id          IS NULL
465:     AND execution_id    IS NULL
466:     AND iee_run_id      IS NULL)
467:     -- source_id is optional for 'system' (may be NULL for truly unattributable
468:     -- platform work, or set to a job/service identifier when attribution exists)
469:);
470:```
471:
472:**CHECK constraint — `executionPhase` nullability invariant:**
473:
474:```sql
475:ALTER TABLE llm_requests ADD CONSTRAINT llm_requests_execution_phase_ck CHECK (
476:  (source_type IN ('agent_run', 'process_execution', 'iee') AND execution_phase IS NOT NULL)
477:  OR
478:  (source_type IN ('system', 'analyzer') AND execution_phase IS NULL)
479:);
480:```
481:
482:**Index additions:**
483:
484:```sql
485:CREATE INDEX llm_requests_source_id_idx          ON llm_requests (source_id) WHERE source_id IS NOT NULL;
486:CREATE INDEX llm_requests_feature_tag_month_idx  ON llm_requests (feature_tag, billing_month);
487:CREATE INDEX llm_requests_status_idx             ON llm_requests (status) WHERE status <> 'success';
488:```
489:
490:The partial index on `status` avoids the common case (success rows, ~99% of traffic) and speeds up debugging queries ("show me all 499s this week").
491:
492:**Drizzle schema update** in [server/db/schema/llmRequests.ts](server/db/schema/llmRequests.ts):
493:
494:- Add four columns.
495:- Extend `SOURCE_TYPES` array with `'analyzer'`.
496:- Extend `LLM_REQUEST_STATUSES` array with `'client_disconnected'`, `'parse_failure'`, `'aborted_by_caller'`.
497:- Change `executionPhase` type from `notNull()` to nullable.
498:- Add TypeScript types for `AbortReason`.
499:
500:See §19 Contracts for the full updated TypeScript types.

293:
294:## 5. Design decisions — the four fault lines
295:
296:Each subsection below names a directional design decision, the decision taken, and the rejected alternatives (with reasons). These are the questions the `spec-reviewer` agent will pause for HITL on if they are implicit — pinning them here prevents that.
297:
298:### 5.1 Attribution pattern — polymorphic `sourceId` vs FK-per-consumer
299:
300:**Decision:** Introduce two new columns on `llm_requests`:
301:
302:- `sourceId uuid` — polymorphic pointer. When populated, points to a row in whichever table `sourceType` names. No referential integrity constraint (FK would have to be to multiple tables).
303:- `sourceType` remains the existing `text` column, but is extended with additional values (see §5.2's adjacent decision).
304:
305:Existing typed FKs (`runId`, `executionId`, `ieeRunId`) are **kept as-is**. They are the primary attribution mechanism for their respective consumers — the polymorphic pattern is *additive*, used only by new consumers who don't have a typed FK.
306:
307:**Assertion that makes this unambiguous:** For any row in `llm_requests`, exactly one of the following holds:
308:
309:- `sourceType = 'agent_run'` AND `runId IS NOT NULL` AND `sourceId IS NULL`
310:- `sourceType = 'process_execution'` AND `executionId IS NOT NULL` AND `sourceId IS NULL`
311:- `sourceType = 'iee'` AND `ieeRunId IS NOT NULL` AND `sourceId IS NULL`
312:- `sourceType IN ('system', 'analyzer', …future values…)` AND `sourceId IS NOT NULL` AND all three typed FKs NULL
313:- `sourceType = 'system'` AND `sourceId IS NULL` (legacy system rows without attribution; preserved for backward compat)
314:
315:Enforced by a database `CHECK` constraint (see §6.1).
316:
317:**Rejected alternatives:**
318:
319:- **Column-per-consumer.** Adding `analyzerJobId` then `workspaceMemoryCompileJobId` then the next one. Schema grows linearly with consumer count. Every addition requires a migration and a backfill. **Rejected as compounding debt.**
320:- **Remove typed FKs, use only polymorphic.** Clean in theory; catastrophic to migrate. Existing queries, existing indexes, existing joins across `agent_runs ↔ llm_requests` would all break. The downside of keeping typed FKs (a bit of schema asymmetry) is much smaller than the cost of a deep rewrite. **Rejected on pragmatism.**
321:- **Junction table `llm_request_sources`.** Would require an extra JOIN on every ledger read. For a high-write table this is measurable. **Rejected on query-path cost.**
322:
323:**Load-bearing mechanism:** the `CHECK` constraint in migration 0180. Without it, the invariant is prose; with it, the invariant is enforced.
324:
325:### 5.2 Taxonomy pattern — `taskType` enum extension vs `featureTag` freeform
326:
327:**Decision:** Keep `taskType` as a closed enum (it already has 10 values). **Do not extend it** for new consumers. Add a new column:
328:
329:- `featureTag text NOT NULL DEFAULT 'unknown'` — freeform kebab-case identifier for the specific LLM use case. Examples: `skill-analyzer-classify`, `skill-analyzer-agent-match`, `skill-analyzer-cluster-recommend`, `workspace-memory-compile`, `belief-extraction`, `hyde-expansion`.
330:
331:Router callers must set it; default `'unknown'` exists only to make the column `NOT NULL` without breaking existing code paths that might silently not yet set it. A static check at the router level logs a warning when a call arrives with `featureTag = 'unknown'` in non-test code.
332:
333:**Why two separate columns (`taskType` + `featureTag`)?** They answer different questions:
334:
335:- `taskType` answers "what class of work is this?" — used by model routing (`resolveLLM()` consumes it).
336:- `featureTag` answers "which feature is this?" — used by cost-attribution dashboards and the System P&L page.
337:
338:A reader of the Usage page wants to see feature-level breakdowns ("how much did the analyzer cost this week?"). A router making model-selection decisions wants to see task-level classes (`general`, `qa_validation`, `memory_compile`). Conflating them into one column makes either one slightly worse at its job.
339:
340:**Rejected alternatives:**
341:
342:- **Extend `taskType` with `skill_classify` etc.** Closed enum = migration per feature = churn. Also conflates routing policy concepts with reporting concepts. **Rejected.**
343:- **Overload `agentName` as a feature tag.** `agentName` is only meaningful for agent runs; using it for non-agent callers would break its existing semantics for the Usage page's "by agent" breakdown. **Rejected.**
344:- **JSONB metadata column.** Too flexible; makes aggregation slow and reporting brittle. **Rejected.**
345:
346:### 5.3 `executionPhase` semantics for non-agent callers
347:
348:**Decision:** Make `executionPhase` nullable. The existing enum (`planning | execution | synthesis | iee_loop_step`) is agent-execution-shaped and doesn't describe "one-shot classifier call" or "background job inference." For non-agent callers:
349:
350:- `executionPhase` is **NULL** when `sourceType ∈ {'system', 'analyzer', plus any future non-agent source}`.
351:- `executionPhase` remains **required (NOT NULL)** when `sourceType ∈ {'agent_run', 'process_execution', 'iee'}`.
352:
353:Enforced by the same `CHECK` constraint as the attribution invariant (§5.1).
354:
355:**Why not add a neutral `'batch'` or `'one_shot'` enum value?** Because that value carries no useful semantics — it means "not agent execution," which is exactly what `NULL` already conveys. Adding a dummy value pollutes every dashboard that groups by phase with a meaningless bucket. NULL-as-absent is the honest representation.
356:
357:**Rejected alternatives:**
358:
359:- **Add `'batch'` value.** Dashboard clutter for zero routing benefit. **Rejected.**
360:- **Reshape `executionPhase` into a more generic `callContext` column.** Breaks every existing query. **Rejected on migration cost.**
361:
362:### 5.4 Router policy for system callers — routing resolution + budget
363:
364:**Decision:** Introduce a new enum on `LLMCallContextSchema` — `systemCallerPolicy: 'respect_routing' | 'bypass_routing'` — defaulting to `'respect_routing'`. When set to `'bypass_routing'`:
365:
366:- `resolveLLM()` is skipped; the caller's chosen `provider` and `model` are used verbatim. `capabilityTier`, `wasDowngraded`, `routingReason` remain populated for reporting (`routingReason = 'forced'`, `wasDowngraded = false`).
367:- `budgetService.checkAndReserve()` is still invoked unconditionally, but its return type is widened to `string | null` and it returns `null` (no reservation) for `sourceType ∈ {'system', 'analyzer'}`. Downstream code already tolerates `null` as "no reservation to release on error", because system calls have no billing line. See §7.2 for the exact branch and §19.10 for the updated contract.
368:
369:**Why bypass routing at all?** The analyzer has legitimate reasons to pin `claude-sonnet-4-6` for classification (the prompt is tuned for that model's JSON parse reliability). Routing would downgrade it to Haiku based on policy, breaking the spec-correctness of the analyzer's output. For migrations, this is exactly the right escape hatch — opt-in, per-call, visible in the ledger.
370:
371:**Why still go through the router (not skip entirely)?** Because the router is the only primitive that writes `llm_requests`. Bypass-routing still writes the row. Skip-router doesn't. That's the whole point of this spec.
372:
373:**Rejected alternatives:**
374:
375:- **Always route — no bypass.** Breaks analyzer correctness; analyzer Sonnet prompts are not Haiku-compatible without redesign. Also breaks any future caller that has a good reason to pin a model. **Rejected.**
376:- **Add a new `resolveLLM` strategy per caller.** Unbounded policy sprawl. **Rejected.**
377:- **Put the bypass inside the adapter.** Moves the decision to the wrong layer; the router is where routing policy belongs. **Rejected.**
378:
379:### 5.5 Summary table
380:
381:| Fault line | Decision | Mechanism | Trade-off accepted |
382:|---|---|---|---|
383:| Attribution pattern | Polymorphic `sourceId` + keep typed FKs | DB `CHECK` constraint | Schema asymmetry (acceptable) |
384:| Taxonomy pattern | New `featureTag` column, keep `taskType` enum | Static check at router call site | Two columns instead of one (intentional) |
385:| `executionPhase` for non-agents | Nullable, NULL for system/analyzer | Same `CHECK` constraint | Removes `NOT NULL` on that column |
386:| Router policy for system | `systemCallerPolicy` enum default `'respect_routing'` | New field on `LLMCallContextSchema` | Per-call opt-out (intentional) |
387:
388:---

390:## 6. Data model changes
391:
392:### 6.1 `llm_requests` schema additions (migration 0180)
393:
394:Four new columns, one loosened constraint, three new `status` values, one extended `sourceType` value set, one new `CHECK` constraint.
395:
396:**Migration file:** `migrations/0180_llm_requests_generalisation.sql`
397:
398:**Column additions:**
399:
400:```sql
401:ALTER TABLE llm_requests
402:  ADD COLUMN source_id uuid,                                -- polymorphic FK (no RI)
403:  ADD COLUMN feature_tag text NOT NULL DEFAULT 'unknown',   -- kebab-case feature identifier
404:  ADD COLUMN parse_failure_raw_excerpt text,                -- ≤2 KB truncated LLM response
405:  ADD COLUMN abort_reason text;                             -- 'caller_timeout' | 'caller_cancel' | NULL
406:```
407:
408:**Constraint changes:**
409:
410:```sql
411:ALTER TABLE llm_requests ALTER COLUMN execution_phase DROP NOT NULL;
412:
413:-- Drop the `sourceType` column default so every insert path MUST specify
414:-- a source_type explicitly. The existing default `'agent_run'` would
415:-- silently satisfy a legacy NULL-runId insert and bypass the new
416:-- attribution CHECK — closing that gap is the entire point of this spec.
417:ALTER TABLE llm_requests ALTER COLUMN source_type DROP DEFAULT;
418:```
419:
420:The schema file `server/db/schema/llmRequests.ts` is updated in the same migration to remove `.default('agent_run')` from the `sourceType` column declaration. Every router insert path already sets `sourceType` explicitly today (verified during P1 — the router always has a `ctx.sourceType`), so the default is unreachable in practice. Dropping it catches the next caller who forgets.
421:
422:**Status enum extensions** (stored as free `text`; enforced by app-level enum in `llmRequests.ts`):
423:
424:- Add `'client_disconnected'` — HTTP 499 equivalent, our side aborted/closed the socket.
425:- Add `'parse_failure'` — provider returned a structurally-OK response that failed our schema check after all retries exhausted.
426:- Add `'aborted_by_caller'` — `AbortController.abort()` fired from caller code (distinct from caller_timeout).
427:
428:**sourceType enum extension** (app-level):
429:
430:- Add `'analyzer'` — skill-analyzer calls after migration.
431:- Keep `'system'` as the generic non-attributed catch-all for future system consumers that don't have their own sourceType value yet.
432:
433:**CHECK constraint — attribution invariant:**
434:
435:Every clause below fully constrains every attribution column so the invariant prose in §5.1 is encoded exactly — no attribution column can appear where it doesn't belong.
436:
437:```sql
438:ALTER TABLE llm_requests ADD CONSTRAINT llm_requests_attribution_ck CHECK (
439:  (source_type = 'agent_run'
440:     AND run_id          IS NOT NULL
441:     AND execution_id    IS NULL
442:     AND iee_run_id      IS NULL
443:     AND source_id       IS NULL)
444:  OR
445:  (source_type = 'process_execution'
446:     AND execution_id    IS NOT NULL
447:     AND run_id          IS NULL
448:     AND iee_run_id      IS NULL
449:     AND source_id       IS NULL)
450:  OR
451:  (source_type = 'iee'
452:     AND iee_run_id      IS NOT NULL
453:     AND run_id          IS NULL
454:     AND execution_id    IS NULL
455:     AND source_id       IS NULL)
456:  OR
457:  (source_type = 'analyzer'
458:     AND source_id       IS NOT NULL
459:     AND run_id          IS NULL
460:     AND execution_id    IS NULL
461:     AND iee_run_id      IS NULL)
462:  OR
463:  (source_type = 'system'
464:     AND run_id          IS NULL
465:     AND execution_id    IS NULL
466:     AND iee_run_id      IS NULL)
467:     -- source_id is optional for 'system' (may be NULL for truly unattributable
468:     -- platform work, or set to a job/service identifier when attribution exists)
469:);
470:```
471:
472:**CHECK constraint — `executionPhase` nullability invariant:**
473:
474:```sql
475:ALTER TABLE llm_requests ADD CONSTRAINT llm_requests_execution_phase_ck CHECK (
476:  (source_type IN ('agent_run', 'process_execution', 'iee') AND execution_phase IS NOT NULL)
477:  OR
478:  (source_type IN ('system', 'analyzer') AND execution_phase IS NULL)
479:);
480:```
481:
482:**Index additions:**
483:
484:```sql
485:CREATE INDEX llm_requests_source_id_idx          ON llm_requests (source_id) WHERE source_id IS NOT NULL;
486:CREATE INDEX llm_requests_feature_tag_month_idx  ON llm_requests (feature_tag, billing_month);
487:CREATE INDEX llm_requests_status_idx             ON llm_requests (status) WHERE status <> 'success';
488:```
489:
490:The partial index on `status` avoids the common case (success rows, ~99% of traffic) and speeds up debugging queries ("show me all 499s this week").
491:
492:**Drizzle schema update** in [server/db/schema/llmRequests.ts](server/db/schema/llmRequests.ts):
493:
494:- Add four columns.
495:- Extend `SOURCE_TYPES` array with `'analyzer'`.
496:- Extend `LLM_REQUEST_STATUSES` array with `'client_disconnected'`, `'parse_failure'`, `'aborted_by_caller'`.
497:- Change `executionPhase` type from `notNull()` to nullable.
498:- Add TypeScript types for `AbortReason`.

502:### 6.2 `cost_aggregates` schema additions (migration 0181)
503:
504:One new value in the `entity_type` text field. No structural change; the upsert key (`entity_type, entity_id, period_type, period_key`) remains unique and unchanged.
505:
506:**Migration file:** `migrations/0181_cost_aggregates_source_type_dimension.sql`
507:
508:```sql
509:-- No DDL required; entity_type is a text column. Documentation only.
510:COMMENT ON COLUMN cost_aggregates.entity_type IS
511:  'organisation | subaccount | run | agent | task_type | provider | platform | execution_phase | source_type | feature_tag';
512:```
513:
514:**Service change:** [server/services/costAggregateService.ts](server/services/costAggregateService.ts) — `upsertAggregates()` adds two new dimension writes per ledger row:
515:
516:- One row keyed by `entity_type='source_type', entity_id=<sourceType value>`.
517:- One row keyed by `entity_type='feature_tag', entity_id=<featureTag value>`.
518:
519:Both follow the same daily/monthly/minute/hour period-type pattern as the existing dimensions. The `cleanOldAggregates()` job continues to purge minute/hour rows after 2h for these new dimensions too — no change required.
520:
521:**Why no new column on `cost_aggregates`?** `entity_type` + `entity_id` is already polymorphic. Adding the new dimensions is a write-path change only; the table shape accommodates them natively.
522:
523:### 6.3 Polymorphic attribution columns — worked example
524:
525:For a skill-analyzer classify call post-migration:
526:
527:```sql
528:INSERT INTO llm_requests (
529:  idempotency_key, organisation_id, source_type, source_id,
530:  feature_tag, provider, model, task_type, execution_phase,
531:  ...tokens, cost, status...
532:) VALUES (
533:  'idem-<hash>', <org-uuid>, 'analyzer', <skill_analyzer_jobs.id>,
534:  'skill-analyzer-classify', 'anthropic', 'claude-sonnet-4-6', 'general', NULL,
535:  ...
536:);
537:```
538:
539:Query "show me all LLM spend on analyzer runs for org X":
540:
541:```sql
542:SELECT SUM(cost_with_margin) FROM llm_requests
543:WHERE organisation_id = $1
544:  AND source_type = 'analyzer'
545:  AND billing_month = $2;
546:```
547:
548:Query "link analyzer ledger rows back to their job":
549:
550:```sql
551:SELECT r.*, j.source_type AS job_source_type, j.created_at AS job_created
552:FROM llm_requests r
553:LEFT JOIN skill_analyzer_jobs j ON r.source_id = j.id AND r.source_type = 'analyzer'
554:WHERE r.feature_tag LIKE 'skill-analyzer-%'
555:ORDER BY r.created_at DESC;
556:```
557:
558:Note the JOIN has no referential integrity — if the analyzer job is deleted, ledger rows survive (financial audit requirement) and `j.source_type` comes back NULL. That is the intended behaviour.
559:
560:### 6.4 New statuses + parse-failure excerpt — capture rules
561:
562:**Status + `abort_reason` mapping (written by the adapter error mapper, recorded by the router):**
563:
564:- `AbortController.abort('caller_timeout')` fires from caller code (timeout path) → `status = 'aborted_by_caller'`, `abort_reason = 'caller_timeout'`.
565:- `AbortController.abort('caller_cancel')` or bare `abort()` fires from caller code (user-cancel path) → `status = 'aborted_by_caller'`, `abort_reason = 'caller_cancel'`.
566:- `fetch` throws a network error and response was mid-body when the socket RST'd (no `AbortError`) → `status = 'client_disconnected'`, `abort_reason` NULL (we don't know which side initiated).
567:- The provider returns HTTP 499 (rare but possible via OpenRouter or some proxies) → `status = 'client_disconnected'`, `abort_reason = 'caller_timeout'` if the call was aborted by us with that reason, else NULL.
568:
569:**`parse_failure`** is written by the caller (router or adapter callsite) when:
570:
571:- The LLM returned a 200 OK with valid JSON at the HTTP layer.
572:- The caller's post-processing (e.g. `skillAnalyzerServicePure.parseClassificationResponseWithMerge`) couldn't parse the content into the expected schema.
573:- `withBackoff` retried up to `maxAttempts`, exhausted retries, and the final attempt still parse-failed.
574:
575:For `parse_failure` rows, `parse_failure_raw_excerpt` is populated with the **last** attempted response's `content` field, truncated to 2 KB (UTF-8-safe truncation — break at the last complete code point, don't produce invalid UTF-8). If shorter than 2 KB, stored as-is.
576:
577:**Rationale for 2 KB:** big enough to see the structural shape of the malformed response (~500 tokens ≈ 6-10 lines of broken JSON), small enough that even millions of parse failures in a quarter don't bloat storage to GBs. The excerpt is for debugging, not reconstruction.
578:
579:**What about the full response?** Intentionally not stored. `responsePayloadHash` remains the immutable proof-of-content field. If someone needs the full body, the Anthropic console has it via the `providerRequestId`.
580:
581:### 6.5 Idempotency key scheme for new source types
582:
583:Existing `generateIdempotencyKey()` at [llmRouter.ts:77-97](server/services/llmRouter.ts#L77) composes from:
584:
585:```
586:organisationId : (runId ?? executionId ?? 'system') : agentName ?? 'no-agent' : taskType : provider : model : messageHash
587:```
588:
589:For new `sourceType = 'analyzer'` calls, the router must change this to:
590:
591:```
592:organisationId : (runId ?? executionId ?? ieeRunId ?? sourceId ?? 'system') : agentName ?? featureTag ?? 'no-agent' : taskType : provider : model : messageHash
593:```
594:
595:The substitution `featureTag ?? 'no-agent'` when `agentName` is null keeps idempotency deduplication meaningful for non-agent callers (two analyzer calls with the same message, same feature tag, same org should dedupe). Without `featureTag` in the key, all non-agent calls for an org would collide on `'no-agent'`.
596:
597:### 6.6 Migration safety
598:
599:Per `docs/spec-context.md` — `migration_safety_tests: defer_until_live_data_exists`. This migration does not require backfill:
600:
601:- New columns are all nullable or have defaults.
602:- Existing rows in a pre-production dev DB already satisfy the new CHECK constraints by construction (the legacy `sourceType = 'system'` rows have null run/execution/iee IDs; agent_run rows have `runId` set; etc.), so the plain `ADD CONSTRAINT ... CHECK (...)` in §6.1 validates against existing rows immediately without risk of lockout. We do **not** use `NOT VALID` + deferred `VALIDATE CONSTRAINT` here — pre-production, immediate validation is the honest contract.
603:- If a legacy row turns out to violate the new CHECK at migration time, the migration fails cleanly and we fix the offending row (or the constraint) before retrying. Commit-and-revert covers this.
604:
605:Pre-production means no staged rollout. Commit-and-revert is the rollback plan.
606:
607:---
608:
609:## 7. Router changes
610:
611:**File:** [server/services/llmRouter.ts](server/services/llmRouter.ts)
612:
613:### 7.1 `LLMCallContextSchema` additions
614:
615:Extend the Zod schema at [llmRouter.ts:34-58](server/services/llmRouter.ts#L34):
616:
617:```ts
618:const LLMCallContextSchema = z.object({
619:  // ...existing fields...
620:
621:  // Polymorphic attribution for non-agent callers
622:  sourceId:             z.string().uuid().optional(),
623:  featureTag:           z.string().min(1).optional(),
624:
625:  // System-caller policy (default is 'respect_routing')
626:  systemCallerPolicy:   z.enum(['respect_routing', 'bypass_routing']).default('respect_routing'),
627:
628:  // Abort signal (not stored; only used for adapter plumbing)
629:  abortSignal:          z.instanceof(AbortSignal).optional(),
630:});
631:```
632:
633:**Runtime validation logic** added to `routeCall()` after the existing IEE guards:
634:
635:```ts
636:// Attribution invariant — matches the DB CHECK constraint
637:if (ctx.sourceType === 'analyzer') {
638:  if (!ctx.sourceId) {
639:    throw new RouterContractError('llmRouter: sourceId is required when sourceType="analyzer"');
640:  }
641:  if (ctx.runId || ctx.executionId || ctx.ieeRunId) {
642:    throw new RouterContractError('llmRouter: analyzer rows must not set agent/execution/iee FKs');
643:  }
644:}
645:
646:// Feature tag hygiene
647:if (!ctx.featureTag) {
648:  logger.warn('llm_router_missing_feature_tag', {
649:    sourceType: ctx.sourceType,
650:    caller: new Error().stack?.split('\n')[3],
651:  });
652:}
653:```
654:
655:### 7.2 System-caller policy (routing + budget)
656:
657:Gate the existing model-resolution path on `systemCallerPolicy`:
658:
659:```ts
660:if (ctx.systemCallerPolicy === 'bypass_routing') {
661:  effectiveProvider = ctx.provider ?? 'anthropic';
662:  effectiveModel = ctx.model ?? 'claude-sonnet-4-6';
663:  routingReason = 'forced';
664:  // Do NOT call resolveLLM() — caller has pinned model+provider.
665:} else {
666:  // Existing resolveLLM() path, unchanged.
667:}
668:```
669:
670:**Budget bypass:** widen the return type of `budgetService.checkAndReserve()` (file: [server/services/budgetService.ts](server/services/budgetService.ts)) from `string` to `string | null` and add an early return:
671:
672:```ts
673:async function checkAndReserve(ctx: LLMCallContext, conn?: TxOrDb): Promise<string | null> {
674:  // System-level work is unbudgeted; return null (no reservation).
675:  if (ctx.sourceType === 'system' || ctx.sourceType === 'analyzer') {
676:    return null;
677:  }
678:  // ...existing logic unchanged, returns a reservation id string...
679:}
680:```
681:
682:Update `llmRouter.routeCall()`'s release path to tolerate `null`:
683:
684:```ts
685:const reservationId = await budgetService.checkAndReserve(ctx, tx); // string | null
686:try {
687:  // ...perform call...
688:} catch (err) {
689:  if (reservationId !== null) {
690:    await budgetService.releaseReservation(reservationId, tx);
691:  }
692:  throw err;
693:}
694:```
695:
696:See §19.10 for the updated contract.
697:
698:**Implementation check required during build:** confirm that today's `checkAndReserve` has no existing caller relying on a non-null `string` return (it doesn't, because today every call path is budgeted). If a caller surfaces that DOES narrow, update it in P1 alongside this change.
699:
700:### 7.3 Idempotency-key scheme
701:
702:Update `generateIdempotencyKey()` at [llmRouter.ts:77-97](server/services/llmRouter.ts#L77) per §6.5. Order-sensitive change: the key format is new, so idempotency keys generated before and after this migration won't collide. Pre-production means no in-flight duplicate-detection concerns — but if they did exist, the right answer would be to include a schema version prefix (`v2:...`). We don't; the format just changes.
703:
704:### 7.4 Margin multiplier for system + analyzer rows
705:
706:`llmRouter.routeCall()` currently resolves `marginMultiplier` from the pricing service (typically `1.30` for billable work). For `sourceType ∈ {'system', 'analyzer'}` the row is not billable — there is no revenue to attach margin to. The router therefore overrides the resolved multiplier to `1.0` on that path:
707:
708:```ts
709:const resolved = await pricingService.resolve(provider, model);
710:const marginMultiplier =
711:  ctx.sourceType === 'system' || ctx.sourceType === 'analyzer'
712:    ? 1.0
713:    : resolved.marginMultiplier;
714:```
715:
716:With `marginMultiplier = 1.0`, `costWithMargin === costRaw` for those rows. The P&L page's "no revenue for system" assertion (§11.5) and the `SourceTypeRow.revenueCents: null` rendering in §19.5 both depend on this. If this branch is omitted, analyzer rows carry the default `1.30` multiplier and the P&L page reports phantom revenue for analyzer work.
717:
718:### 7.5 What the router does NOT change
719:
720:- No changes to `resolveLLM()` — pure model-selection logic stays the same for agent callers.
721:- No changes to `pricingService` — pricing is provider/model-keyed, not caller-keyed. The margin override in §7.4 is applied at the router level after pricing resolves, not inside `pricingService`.
722:- No changes to the Anthropic request-id capture path — already working, reused verbatim.
723:- No changes to fallback chain logic — provider fallback for analyzer calls works the same as for agent calls.
724:

732:

744:**Adapter implementation (Anthropic):**

746:```ts
747:const response = await fetch('https://api.anthropic.com/v1/messages', {
748:  method: 'POST',
749:  headers: { /* ... */ },
750:  body: JSON.stringify(body),
