501:
502:### 6.2 `cost_aggregates` schema additions (migration 0181)
503:
504:One new value in the `entity_type` text field. No structural change; the upsert key (`entity_type, entity_id, period_type, period_key`) remains unique and unchanged.
505:
506:**Migration file:** `migrations/0181_cost_aggregates_source_type_dimension.sql`
507:
508:```sql
509:-- No DDL required; entity_type is a text column. Documentation only.
510:COMMENT ON COLUMN cost_aggregates.entity_type IS
511:  'organisation | subaccount | run | agent | task_type | provider | platform | execution_phase | source_type | feature_tag';
512:```
513:
514:**Service change:** [server/services/costAggregateService.ts](server/services/costAggregateService.ts) — `upsertAggregates()` adds two new dimension writes per ledger row:
515:
516:- One row keyed by `entity_type='source_type', entity_id=<sourceType value>`.
517:- One row keyed by `entity_type='feature_tag', entity_id=<featureTag value>`.
518:
519:Both follow the same daily/monthly/minute/hour period-type pattern as the existing dimensions. The `cleanOldAggregates()` job continues to purge minute/hour rows after 2h for these new dimensions too — no change required.
520:
521:**Why no new column on `cost_aggregates`?** `entity_type` + `entity_id` is already polymorphic. Adding the new dimensions is a write-path change only; the table shape accommodates them natively.
522:
523:### 6.3 Polymorphic attribution columns — worked example
524:
525:For a skill-analyzer classify call post-migration:
526:
527:```sql
528:INSERT INTO llm_requests (
529:  idempotency_key, organisation_id, source_type, source_id,
530:  feature_tag, provider, model, task_type, execution_phase,
531:  ...tokens, cost, status...
532:) VALUES (
533:  'idem-<hash>', <org-uuid>, 'analyzer', <skill_analyzer_jobs.id>,
534:  'skill-analyzer-classify', 'anthropic', 'claude-sonnet-4-6', 'general', NULL,
535:  ...
536:);
537:```
538:
539:Query "show me all LLM spend on analyzer runs for org X":
540:
541:```sql
542:SELECT SUM(cost_with_margin) FROM llm_requests
543:WHERE organisation_id = $1
544:  AND source_type = 'analyzer'
545:  AND billing_month = $2;
546:```
547:
548:Query "link analyzer ledger rows back to their job":
549:
550:```sql
551:SELECT r.*, j.source_type AS job_source_type, j.created_at AS job_created
552:FROM llm_requests r
553:LEFT JOIN skill_analyzer_jobs j ON r.source_id = j.id AND r.source_type = 'analyzer'
554:WHERE r.feature_tag LIKE 'skill-analyzer-%'
555:ORDER BY r.created_at DESC;
556:```
557:
558:Note the JOIN has no referential integrity — if the analyzer job is deleted, ledger rows survive (financial audit requirement) and `j.source_type` comes back NULL. That is the intended behaviour.
559:
560:### 6.4 New statuses + parse-failure excerpt — capture rules
561:
562:**Status + `abort_reason` mapping (written by the adapter error mapper, recorded by the router):**
563:
564:- `AbortController.abort('caller_timeout')` fires from caller code (timeout path) → `status = 'aborted_by_caller'`, `abort_reason = 'caller_timeout'`.
565:- `AbortController.abort('caller_cancel')` or bare `abort()` fires from caller code (user-cancel path) → `status = 'aborted_by_caller'`, `abort_reason = 'caller_cancel'`.
566:- `fetch` throws a network error and response was mid-body when the socket RST'd (no `AbortError`) → `status = 'client_disconnected'`, `abort_reason` NULL (we don't know which side initiated).
567:- The provider returns HTTP 499 (rare but possible via OpenRouter or some proxies) → `status = 'client_disconnected'`, `abort_reason = 'caller_timeout'` if the call was aborted by us with that reason, else NULL.
568:
569:**`parse_failure`** is written by the caller (router or adapter callsite) when:
570:
571:- The LLM returned a 200 OK with valid JSON at the HTTP layer.
572:- The caller's post-processing (e.g. `skillAnalyzerServicePure.parseClassificationResponseWithMerge`) couldn't parse the content into the expected schema.
573:- `withBackoff` retried up to `maxAttempts`, exhausted retries, and the final attempt still parse-failed.
574:
575:For `parse_failure` rows, `parse_failure_raw_excerpt` is populated with the **last** attempted response's `content` field, truncated to 2 KB (UTF-8-safe truncation — break at the last complete code point, don't produce invalid UTF-8). If shorter than 2 KB, stored as-is.
576:
577:**Rationale for 2 KB:** big enough to see the structural shape of the malformed response (~500 tokens ≈ 6-10 lines of broken JSON), small enough that even millions of parse failures in a quarter don't bloat storage to GBs. The excerpt is for debugging, not reconstruction.
578:
579:**What about the full response?** Intentionally not stored. `responsePayloadHash` remains the immutable proof-of-content field. If someone needs the full body, the Anthropic console has it via the `providerRequestId`.
580:
581:### 6.5 Idempotency key scheme for new source types
582:
583:Existing `generateIdempotencyKey()` at [llmRouter.ts:77-97](server/services/llmRouter.ts#L77) composes from:
584:
585:```
586:organisationId : (runId ?? executionId ?? 'system') : agentName ?? 'no-agent' : taskType : provider : model : messageHash
587:```
588:
589:For new `sourceType = 'analyzer'` calls, the router must change this to:
590:
591:```
592:organisationId : (runId ?? executionId ?? ieeRunId ?? sourceId ?? 'system') : agentName ?? featureTag ?? 'no-agent' : taskType : provider : model : messageHash
593:```
594:
595:The substitution `featureTag ?? 'no-agent'` when `agentName` is null keeps idempotency deduplication meaningful for non-agent callers (two analyzer calls with the same message, same feature tag, same org should dedupe). Without `featureTag` in the key, all non-agent calls for an org would collide on `'no-agent'`.
596:
597:### 6.6 Migration safety
598:
599:Per `docs/spec-context.md` — `migration_safety_tests: defer_until_live_data_exists`. This migration does not require backfill:
600:
601:- New columns are all nullable or have defaults.
602:- Existing rows in a pre-production dev DB already satisfy the new CHECK constraints by construction (the legacy `sourceType = 'system'` rows have null run/execution/iee IDs; agent_run rows have `runId` set; etc.), so the plain `ADD CONSTRAINT ... CHECK (...)` in §6.1 validates against existing rows immediately without risk of lockout. We do **not** use `NOT VALID` + deferred `VALIDATE CONSTRAINT` here — pre-production, immediate validation is the honest contract.
603:- If a legacy row turns out to violate the new CHECK at migration time, the migration fails cleanly and we fix the offending row (or the constraint) before retrying. Commit-and-revert covers this.
604:
605:Pre-production means no staged rollout. Commit-and-revert is the rollback plan.
606:
607:---

727:## 8. Adapter changes
728:
729:**Files:** every adapter registered in `server/services/providers/registry.ts` — [server/services/providers/anthropicAdapter.ts](server/services/providers/anthropicAdapter.ts), [server/services/providers/openaiAdapter.ts](server/services/providers/openaiAdapter.ts), [server/services/providers/geminiAdapter.ts](server/services/providers/geminiAdapter.ts), [server/services/providers/openrouterAdapter.ts](server/services/providers/openrouterAdapter.ts).
730:
731:All four adapters receive the same three changes (signal threading, 499 mapping, AbortError mapping) so A1's "universal observability" claim holds for every provider the registry exposes. §8.4 tracks adapter-by-adapter parity.
732:
733:### 8.1 `AbortController` plumbing
734:
735:**`ProviderCallParams` gains one field:**
736:
737:```ts
738:export interface ProviderCallParams {
739:  // ...existing fields...
740:  signal?: AbortSignal;
741:}
742:```
743:
744:**Adapter implementation (Anthropic):**
745:
746:```ts
747:const response = await fetch('https://api.anthropic.com/v1/messages', {
748:  method: 'POST',
749:  headers: { /* ... */ },
750:  body: JSON.stringify(body),

exec
"C:\\Windows\\System32\\WindowsPowerShell\\v1.0\\powershell.exe" -Command 'rg -n "''^" "tasks/llm-observability-ledger-generalisation-spec.md" | Select-Object -Skip 750 -First 250' in C:\Files\Projects\automation-v1
exec
"C:\\Windows\\System32\\WindowsPowerShell\\v1.0\\powershell.exe" -Command 'rg -n "''^" "tasks/llm-observability-ledger-generalisation-spec.md" | Select-Object -Skip 1000 -First 250' in C:\Files\Projects\automation-v1
exec
"C:\\Windows\\System32\\WindowsPowerShell\\v1.0\\powershell.exe" -Command 'rg -n "''^" "tasks/llm-observability-ledger-generalisation-spec.md" | Select-Object -Skip 1250 -First 250' in C:\Files\Projects\automation-v1

Wall time: 0.4 seconds
Output:
751:  signal: params.signal,   // NEW — threads the abort signal through
752:});
753:```
754:
755:**Error mapping:** if `fetch` throws with `err.name === 'AbortError'`, the adapter reads the `AbortSignal.reason` to preserve the caller's intent (timeout vs manual cancel). This is the load-bearing mechanism that keeps `caller_timeout` and `caller_cancel` distinguishable — without it, every abort collapses to the same reason.
756:
757:The caller uses `AbortController.abort(reason)` with one of the sentinel string values `'caller_timeout'` or `'caller_cancel'`. The adapter then maps:
758:
759:```ts
760:if (err instanceof Error && err.name === 'AbortError') {
761:  // AbortSignal.reason carries whatever was passed to controller.abort(reason).
762:  // Convention: callers pass the string 'caller_timeout' or 'caller_cancel'.
763:  const reasonRaw = params.signal?.reason;
764:  const abortReason: 'caller_timeout' | 'caller_cancel' =
765:    reasonRaw === 'caller_timeout' ? 'caller_timeout' : 'caller_cancel';
766:  throw {
767:    statusCode: 499,
768:    code: 'CLIENT_DISCONNECTED',
769:    provider: 'anthropic',
770:    message: `Request aborted by caller (${abortReason})`,
771:    abortReason,
772:  };
773:}
774:```
775:
776:The router catches this shape and records `status = 'aborted_by_caller'` with `abort_reason` set from `err.abortReason`.
777:
778:**Caller convention (enforced by code review, not a runtime check):** callers that support timeout cancellation pass `abortController.abort('caller_timeout')` from their timeout handler, and pass `abortController.abort('caller_cancel')` (or a bare `abort()` which defaults to `caller_cancel`) from user-initiated cancellation paths. The analyzer migration in §10 wires the `caller_timeout` path exactly — it does not add a new UI-cancel hook. User-cancel (`caller_cancel`) remains a forward-looking abort-reason value in the CHECK constraint; wiring a UI/job-level cancel path into the analyzer's `AbortController` is deferred (§17).
779:
780:**Router-side usage:** `routeCall()` passes `ctx.abortSignal` through to the adapter as `params.signal`. The analyzer migration (§10) creates an `AbortController` per classify call and wires it up.
781:
782:### 8.2 HTTP 499 detection + `client_disconnected` mapping
783:
784:HTTP 499 is rare in direct provider calls (Anthropic doesn't emit it), but can surface via OpenRouter or corporate proxies. Add the mapping defensively:
785:
786:```ts
787:if (response.status === 499) {
788:  throw {
789:    statusCode: 499,
790:    code: 'CLIENT_DISCONNECTED',
791:    provider: 'anthropic',
792:    message: `Client disconnected: ${errorDetail}`,
793:  };
794:}
795:```
796:
797:### 8.3 Parse-failure excerpt capture
798:
799:This is **not an adapter change** — the adapter returns the raw content string. The parse-failure excerpt is captured at the caller site (router or caller of router). Specifically:
800:
801:**Pattern for structured-output callers** (the analyzer, workspace-memory, future callers):
802:
803:```ts
804:try {
805:  const response = await llmRouter.routeCall({ /* ... */ });
806:  const parsed = parseResponseWithSchema(response.content);
807:  if (parsed === null) {
808:    // Parse failure — record the excerpt
809:    throw new ParseFailureError({
810:      status: 'parse_failure',
811:      rawExcerpt: truncateUtf8Safe(response.content, 2048),
812:    });
813:  }
814:  return parsed;
815:} catch (err) {
816:  // The router writes the llm_requests row with parse_failure status
817:  // and rawExcerpt populated. Caller re-raises for control flow.
818:  throw err;
819:}
820:```
821:
822:**Router-side change:** `routeCall()` catches `ParseFailureError` from a caller-supplied post-processor hook. Since the current router doesn't have such a hook, this spec adds one:
823:
824:```ts
825:export interface RouterCallParams {
826:  // ...existing fields...
827:  /** If provided, runs after response is received. Throwing ParseFailureError
828:   *  causes the router to record status='parse_failure' + rawExcerpt and
829:   *  re-throw for caller control flow. */
830:  postProcess?: (content: string) => void;
831:}
832:```
833:
834:For the analyzer, `postProcess` wraps `parseClassificationResponseWithMerge` and throws `ParseFailureError` with the truncated raw excerpt when the parse returns null.
835:
836:**Why at the router, not the adapter?** The adapter doesn't know the caller's schema. The router doesn't either, but it owns the ledger write — so the right split is: caller supplies the post-processor; router owns the record.
837:
838:### 8.4 Parity across adapters
839:
840:All four registered adapters get identical updates in P1:
841:
842:| Adapter | File | Signal threading | 499 mapping | AbortError + reason mapping |
843:|---|---|---|---|---|
844:| Anthropic | `server/services/providers/anthropicAdapter.ts` | Yes | Yes | Yes |
845:| OpenAI | `server/services/providers/openaiAdapter.ts` | Yes | Yes | Yes |
846:| Gemini | `server/services/providers/geminiAdapter.ts` | Yes | Yes | Yes |
847:| OpenRouter | `server/services/providers/openrouterAdapter.ts` | Yes | Yes | Yes |
848:
849:The three changes are:
850:
851:- `signal` param threading through `fetch` (§8.1)
852:- `AbortError → 499 CLIENT_DISCONNECTED` mapping that reads `AbortSignal.reason` to preserve `caller_timeout` vs `caller_cancel` (§8.1)
853:- HTTP 499 → CLIENT_DISCONNECTED mapping (§8.2)
854:
855:The pattern is mechanical and identical across all four adapters. If any adapter lacks a discrete error-mapping seam today, P1 adds one so the shape (`{statusCode, code, provider, message, abortReason?}`) is consistent across the fleet. The router only has to understand one error shape.
856:
857:All four adapters already produce `ProviderResponse` with the same shape (`content`, `tokensIn`, `tokensOut`, `stopReason`, `providerRequestId`) — no additions needed there.
858:
859:**Why all four, not just the two analyzer-relevant ones:** A1 in §1.2 makes a universal-observability claim gated by `verify-no-direct-adapter-calls.sh`. If the gate and the adapter changes only cover two providers, a future caller of `geminiAdapter` or `openrouterAdapter` could silently bypass the ledger and A1 would hold false. Universal means universal — §1.1 sets this expectation, so P1 delivers it for every provider currently in the registry.
860:
861:### 8.5 What the adapter layer does NOT change
862:
863:- No changes to the fetch URL, headers, or request body shape — wire format is identical.
864:- No changes to cost math — `tokensIn/Out` capture stays as-is.
865:- No changes to prompt-caching behaviour — cache_control breakpoints on the Anthropic adapter stay verbatim.
866:- No new adapter added — this spec is additive to the four adapters already registered in `server/services/providers/registry.ts`.
867:
868:---
869:
870:## 9. Direct-adapter caller sweep
871:
872:### 9.1 Methodology
873:
874:Run targeted greps across every registered provider adapter — the four files in `server/services/providers/registry.ts` — to enumerate every file outside `server/services/llmRouter.ts` and `server/services/providers/*.ts` that calls an adapter directly:
875:
876:```bash
877:# Direct adapter imports (all four providers)
878:grep -rnE "from.*providers/(anthropic|openai|gemini|openrouter)Adapter" server/ --include='*.ts' \
879:  | grep -v 'llmRouter.ts' | grep -v '/providers/' | grep -v '\.test\.ts'
880:
881:# Explicit call sites (all four providers)
882:grep -rnE "(anthropicAdapter|openaiAdapter|geminiAdapter|openrouterAdapter)\.call" server/ --include='*.ts' \
883:  | grep -v 'llmRouter.ts' | grep -v '/providers/' | grep -v '\.test\.ts'
884:```
885:
886:Each hit is a caller that bypasses the ledger. If `server/services/providers/registry.ts` gains a fifth adapter later, the grep patterns and the gate whitelist are updated together — see §9.4.
887:
888:### 9.2 Known hits (at time of spec authoring)
889:
890:Based on conversation-time reconnaissance:
891:
892:| File | Lines | What it does | Action |
893:|---|---|---|---|
894:| `server/jobs/skillAnalyzerJob.ts` | 768, 1321, 1459 | Classify call, Haiku agent-match, Sonnet cluster-recommend | Migrate (§10.1, §10.2, §10.3) |
895:| `server/services/skillAnalyzerService.ts` | 2063 | Analyzer service-layer direct adapter call | Migrate (§10.4) |
896:
897:All four analyzer subsystem sites are migrated in P3. A1 in §1.2 is verifiable only after this phase: the static gate at §9.4 removes every analyzer file from its whitelist once P3 lands.
898:
899:Other potential callers need confirmation during Phase 2. Candidates to verify:
900:
901:- `server/services/workspaceMemoryService.ts` — HyDE query expansion + context enrichment (already routes through the router per `llmRequests.taskType` values `hyde_expansion` + `context_enrichment`, but this needs confirmation).
902:- `server/services/beliefExtractionService.ts` or equivalent — agent-beliefs extraction (taskType `belief_extraction` exists, likely routed).
903:
904:Any caller confirmed as bypassing during the Phase 2 audit is either migrated in the same phase (if small) or documented as Phase 5 cleanup in §15.
905:
906:### 9.3 Remediation pattern
907:
908:Every migrated caller follows the same shape:
909:
910:**Before:**
911:```ts
912:const response = await anthropicAdapter.call({
913:  model: 'claude-sonnet-4-6',
914:  system: '...',
915:  messages: [...],
916:  maxTokens: 8192,
917:  temperature: 0.1,
918:});
919:```
920:
921:**After:**
922:```ts
923:const response = await llmRouter.routeCall({
924:  system: '...',
925:  messages: [...],
926:  maxTokens: 8192,
927:  temperature: 0.1,
928:  context: {
929:    organisationId: job.organisationId,
930:    sourceType: 'analyzer',               // or 'system' for truly non-attributable
931:    sourceId: job.id,                     // polymorphic FK
932:    featureTag: 'skill-analyzer-classify',
933:    taskType: 'general',
934:    systemCallerPolicy: 'bypass_routing', // opt-out of auto-routing (analyzer pins Sonnet)
935:    provider: 'anthropic',
936:    model: 'claude-sonnet-4-6',
937:    abortSignal: abortController.signal,
938:  },
939:});
940:```
941:
942:The migration is mechanical. The only judgment calls per caller are:
943:
944:1. `sourceType` — use `'analyzer'` for analyzer work, `'system'` for anything else non-attributable.
945:2. `featureTag` — kebab-case unique identifier.
946:3. `systemCallerPolicy` — `'bypass_routing'` if the caller has a specific model pinned; `'respect_routing'` (default) if the caller is OK with router-selected models.
947:
948:### 9.4 Static gate — `verify-no-direct-adapter-calls.sh`
949:
950:**File:** `scripts/gates/verify-no-direct-adapter-calls.sh` (new)
951:
952:**Behaviour:**
953:
954:- Greps the same patterns as §9.1 — covering every adapter registered in `server/services/providers/registry.ts` (today: `anthropic`, `openai`, `gemini`, `openrouter`).
955:- Exits non-zero if any hit is found outside the whitelist (`server/services/llmRouter.ts`, `server/services/providers/*.ts`, any `*.test.ts` or `*.test.tsx`).
956:- Registered in `scripts/run-all-gates.sh` so CI fails on regression.
957:- Whitelist lives at the top of the script as an explicit bash array — no config file, no env vars.
958:- Adapter list lives at the top of the script as a separate bash array. When a new provider adapter is added, the array is updated in the same commit — the gate auto-expands its grep patterns from the array.
959:
960:Prevents the next contributor from re-introducing the pattern the whole spec is designed to eliminate, across every provider adapter the registry exposes.
961:
962:---
963:
964:## 10. Skill-analyzer migration
965:
966:The analyzer is the proof-of-concept consumer. After this phase, every analyzer LLM call shows up in the ledger.
967:
968:### 10.1 Classify call — `skillAnalyzerJob.ts:768`
969:
970:Current state (3-way direct call wrapped in `withBackoff`):
971:
972:```ts
973:const response = await anthropicAdapter.call({
974:  model: 'claude-sonnet-4-6',
975:  system, messages: [{ role: 'user', content: userMessage }],
976:  maxTokens: 8192, temperature: 0.1,
977:});
978:const parsed = skillAnalyzerServicePure.parseClassificationResponseWithMerge(response.content);
979:```
980:
981:Target state:
982:
983:```ts
984:const abortController = new AbortController();
985:// Pass 'caller_timeout' as the reason so the adapter can distinguish
986:// "analyzer-side timeout" from "user-initiated cancel" (see §8.1).
987:const timeoutId = setTimeout(
988:  () => abortController.abort('caller_timeout'),
989:  SKILL_CLASSIFY_TIMEOUT_MS,
990:);
991:
992:try {
993:  const response = await llmRouter.routeCall({
994:    system,
995:    messages: [{ role: 'user', content: userMessage }],
996:    maxTokens: 8192,
997:    temperature: 0.1,
998:    context: {
999:      organisationId: job.organisationId,
1000:      sourceType: 'analyzer',

 exited 1 in 429ms:
751:  signal: params.signal,   // NEW — threads the abort signal through
752:});
753:```
754:
755:**Error mapping:** if `fetch` throws with `err.name === 'AbortError'`, the adapter reads the `AbortSignal.reason` to preserve the caller's intent (timeout vs manual cancel). This is the load-bearing mechanism that keeps `caller_timeout` and `caller_cancel` distinguishable — without it, every abort collapses to the same reason.
756:
757:The caller uses `AbortController.abort(reason)` with one of the sentinel string values `'caller_timeout'` or `'caller_cancel'`. The adapter then maps:
758:
759:```ts
760:if (err instanceof Error && err.name === 'AbortError') {
761:  // AbortSignal.reason carries whatever was passed to controller.abort(reason).
762:  // Convention: callers pass the string 'caller_timeout' or 'caller_cancel'.
763:  const reasonRaw = params.signal?.reason;
764:  const abortReason: 'caller_timeout' | 'caller_cancel' =
765:    reasonRaw === 'caller_timeout' ? 'caller_timeout' : 'caller_cancel';
766:  throw {
767:    statusCode: 499,
768:    code: 'CLIENT_DISCONNECTED',
769:    provider: 'anthropic',
770:    message: `Request aborted by caller (${abortReason})`,
771:    abortReason,
772:  };
773:}
774:```
775:
776:The router catches this shape and records `status = 'aborted_by_caller'` with `abort_reason` set from `err.abortReason`.
777:
778:**Caller convention (enforced by code review, not a runtime check):** callers that support timeout cancellation pass `abortController.abort('caller_timeout')` from their timeout handler, and pass `abortController.abort('caller_cancel')` (or a bare `abort()` which defaults to `caller_cancel`) from user-initiated cancellation paths. The analyzer migration in §10 wires the `caller_timeout` path exactly — it does not add a new UI-cancel hook. User-cancel (`caller_cancel`) remains a forward-looking abort-reason value in the CHECK constraint; wiring a UI/job-level cancel path into the analyzer's `AbortController` is deferred (§17).
779:
780:**Router-side usage:** `routeCall()` passes `ctx.abortSignal` through to the adapter as `params.signal`. The analyzer migration (§10) creates an `AbortController` per classify call and wires it up.
781:
782:### 8.2 HTTP 499 detection + `client_disconnected` mapping
783:
784:HTTP 499 is rare in direct provider calls (Anthropic doesn't emit it), but can surface via OpenRouter or corporate proxies. Add the mapping defensively:
785:
786:```ts
787:if (response.status === 499) {
788:  throw {
789:    statusCode: 499,
790:    code: 'CLIENT_DISCONNECTED',
791:    provider: 'anthropic',
792:    message: `Client disconnected: ${errorDetail}`,
793:  };
794:}
795:```
796:
797:### 8.3 Parse-failure excerpt capture
798:
799:This is **not an adapter change** — the adapter returns the raw content string. The parse-failure excerpt is captured at the caller site (router or caller of router). Specifically:
800:
801:**Pattern for structured-output callers** (the analyzer, workspace-memory, future callers):
802:
803:```ts
804:try {
805:  const response = await llmRouter.routeCall({ /* ... */ });
806:  const parsed = parseResponseWithSchema(response.content);
807:  if (parsed === null) {
808:    // Parse failure — record the excerpt
809:    throw new ParseFailureError({
810:      status: 'parse_failure',
811:      rawExcerpt: truncateUtf8Safe(response.content, 2048),
812:    });
813:  }
814:  return parsed;
815:} catch (err) {
816:  // The router writes the llm_requests row with parse_failure status
817:  // and rawExcerpt populated. Caller re-raises for control flow.
818:  throw err;
819:}
820:```
821:
822:**Router-side change:** `routeCall()` catches `ParseFailureError` from a caller-supplied post-processor hook. Since the current router doesn't have such a hook, this spec adds one:
823:
824:```ts
825:export interface RouterCallParams {
826:  // ...existing fields...
827:  /** If provided, runs after response is received. Throwing ParseFailureError
828:   *  causes the router to record status='parse_failure' + rawExcerpt and
829:   *  re-throw for caller control flow. */
830:  postProcess?: (content: string) => void;
831:}
832:```
833:
834:For the analyzer, `postProcess` wraps `parseClassificationResponseWithMerge` and throws `ParseFailureError` with the truncated raw excerpt when the parse returns null.
835:
836:**Why at the router, not the adapter?** The adapter doesn't know the caller's schema. The router doesn't either, but it owns the ledger write — so the right split is: caller supplies the post-processor; router owns the record.
837:
838:### 8.4 Parity across adapters
839:
840:All four registered adapters get identical updates in P1:
841:
842:| Adapter | File | Signal threading | 499 mapping | AbortError + reason mapping |
843:|---|---|---|---|---|
844:| Anthropic | `server/services/providers/anthropicAdapter.ts` | Yes | Yes | Yes |
845:| OpenAI | `server/services/providers/openaiAdapter.ts` | Yes | Yes | Yes |
846:| Gemini | `server/services/providers/geminiAdapter.ts` | Yes | Yes | Yes |
847:| OpenRouter | `server/services/providers/openrouterAdapter.ts` | Yes | Yes | Yes |
848:
849:The three changes are:
850:
851:- `signal` param threading through `fetch` (§8.1)
852:- `AbortError → 499 CLIENT_DISCONNECTED` mapping that reads `AbortSignal.reason` to preserve `caller_timeout` vs `caller_cancel` (§8.1)
853:- HTTP 499 → CLIENT_DISCONNECTED mapping (§8.2)
854:
855:The pattern is mechanical and identical across all four adapters. If any adapter lacks a discrete error-mapping seam today, P1 adds one so the shape (`{statusCode, code, provider, message, abortReason?}`) is consistent across the fleet. The router only has to understand one error shape.
856:
857:All four adapters already produce `ProviderResponse` with the same shape (`content`, `tokensIn`, `tokensOut`, `stopReason`, `providerRequestId`) — no additions needed there.
858:
859:**Why all four, not just the two analyzer-relevant ones:** A1 in §1.2 makes a universal-observability claim gated by `verify-no-direct-adapter-calls.sh`. If the gate and the adapter changes only cover two providers, a future caller of `geminiAdapter` or `openrouterAdapter` could silently bypass the ledger and A1 would hold false. Universal means universal — §1.1 sets this expectation, so P1 delivers it for every provider currently in the registry.
860:
861:### 8.5 What the adapter layer does NOT change
862:
863:- No changes to the fetch URL, headers, or request body shape — wire format is identical.
864:- No changes to cost math — `tokensIn/Out` capture stays as-is.
865:- No changes to prompt-caching behaviour — cache_control breakpoints on the Anthropic adapter stay verbatim.
866:- No new adapter added — this spec is additive to the four adapters already registered in `server/services/providers/registry.ts`.
867:

963:
964:## 10. Skill-analyzer migration
965:
966:The analyzer is the proof-of-concept consumer. After this phase, every analyzer LLM call shows up in the ledger.
967:
968:### 10.1 Classify call — `skillAnalyzerJob.ts:768`
969:
970:Current state (3-way direct call wrapped in `withBackoff`):
971:
972:```ts
973:const response = await anthropicAdapter.call({
974:  model: 'claude-sonnet-4-6',
975:  system, messages: [{ role: 'user', content: userMessage }],
976:  maxTokens: 8192, temperature: 0.1,
977:});
978:const parsed = skillAnalyzerServicePure.parseClassificationResponseWithMerge(response.content);
979:```
980:
981:Target state:
982:
983:```ts
984:const abortController = new AbortController();
985:// Pass 'caller_timeout' as the reason so the adapter can distinguish
986:// "analyzer-side timeout" from "user-initiated cancel" (see §8.1).
987:const timeoutId = setTimeout(
988:  () => abortController.abort('caller_timeout'),
989:  SKILL_CLASSIFY_TIMEOUT_MS,
990:);
991:
992:try {
993:  const response = await llmRouter.routeCall({
994:    system,
995:    messages: [{ role: 'user', content: userMessage }],
996:    maxTokens: 8192,
997:    temperature: 0.1,
998:    context: {
999:      organisationId: job.organisationId,
1000:      sourceType: 'analyzer',

 exited 1 in 430ms:
1001:      sourceId: job.id,
1002:      featureTag: 'skill-analyzer-classify',
1003:      taskType: 'general',
1004:      systemCallerPolicy: 'bypass_routing',
1005:      provider: 'anthropic',
1006:      model: 'claude-sonnet-4-6',
1007:      abortSignal: abortController.signal,
1008:    },
1009:    postProcess: (content) => {
1010:      const parsed = skillAnalyzerServicePure.parseClassificationResponseWithMerge(content);
1011:      if (parsed === null) {
1012:        throw new ParseFailureError({
1013:          rawExcerpt: truncateUtf8Safe(content, 2048),
1014:        });
1015:      }
1016:    },
1017:  });
1018:  return skillAnalyzerServicePure.parseClassificationResponseWithMerge(response.content);
1019:} finally {
1020:  clearTimeout(timeoutId);
1021:}
1022:```
1023:
1024:Replace the existing `Promise.race([withBackoff(...), timeoutPromise])` pattern with the `AbortController` pattern — they do the same thing, but the latter actually kills the underlying fetch (see §2.3).
1025:
1026:**`withBackoff` retention:** `routeCall` internally uses its own retry strategy via the router's fallback-chain logic. The analyzer's current `maxAttempts: 3` for parse failures specifically is handled by the `postProcess` hook re-throwing `ParseFailureError`, which the router's retry policy classifies as retryable (same classification the analyzer uses today — 429, 503, 529, PARSE_FAILURE).
1027:
1028:### 10.2 Haiku agent-suggestion call — `skillAnalyzerJob.ts:1321`
1029:
1030:Similar migration. Different `featureTag` (`skill-analyzer-agent-match`), different model (`claude-haiku-4-5-20251001`), same general shape.
1031:
1032:### 10.3 Sonnet cluster-recommendation call — `skillAnalyzerJob.ts:1459`
1033:
1034:Third migration. `featureTag: 'skill-analyzer-cluster-recommend'`. Same shape.
1035:
1036:### 10.4 Service-layer call — `skillAnalyzerService.ts:2063`
1037:
1038:Fourth migration. Same mechanical shape as §10.1–§10.3. Replace the direct `anthropicAdapter.call()` invocation at `server/services/skillAnalyzerService.ts:2063` with `llmRouter.routeCall()`.
1039:
1040:- `sourceType: 'analyzer'`.
1041:- `sourceId` — `skill_analyzer_jobs.id` of the enclosing analyzer job. Per the analyzer-row invariant in §6.3, `sourceType='analyzer'` means `llm_requests.source_id` joins cleanly to `skill_analyzer_jobs.id`; all four analyzer sites (three job-layer, one service-layer) must honour that invariant so the P&L page's drawer link-back to the job works deterministically. If the call site does not have a job id in scope today, thread one through from the job that invokes the service (every code path that reaches `skillAnalyzerService.ts:2063` is started by a `skillAnalyzerJob.ts` run, so the id is available upstream).
1042:- `featureTag` — pick a stable kebab-case tag that distinguishes this site from the three job-layer sites (e.g. `skill-analyzer-service-<operation>`, where `<operation>` reflects the specific call the service is making; the exact tag is chosen at implementation time once the site's context is in hand).
1043:- `systemCallerPolicy` — `'bypass_routing'` if the site pins a specific model today; otherwise `'respect_routing'`.
1044:- Thread the existing `AbortController` / `AbortSignal` through to `llmRouter.routeCall()` per §8.1.
1045:
1046:### 10.5 Verification
1047:
1048:After the four migrations, run the analyzer end-to-end on a test import and verify:
1049:
1050:1. `SELECT COUNT(*) FROM llm_requests WHERE feature_tag LIKE 'skill-analyzer-%' AND created_at > <before_test>` returns a non-zero count roughly equal to the number of candidates × number of LLM calls per candidate (summed across the three job-layer sites and the service-layer site from §10.4).
1051:2. Cross-check `providerRequestId` values against the Anthropic console — every row's provider_request_id should match an entry in Anthropic's log (within a tolerance for the specific request).
1052:3. `SELECT SUM(cost_with_margin) FROM llm_requests WHERE feature_tag LIKE 'skill-analyzer-%' AND billing_month = '2026-MM'` gives a non-zero total that appears in `cost_aggregates` rolled up under `entity_type = 'feature_tag'`.
1053:4. Let a classify timeout via its existing `SKILL_CLASSIFY_TIMEOUT_MS` path and verify the resulting ledger row carries `status = 'aborted_by_caller'` and `abort_reason = 'caller_timeout'`.
1054:5. Simulate a parse failure by temporarily breaking the schema validator and verify `parseFailureRawExcerpt` is populated ≤2 KB.
1055:
1056:Verification is manual during Phase 3 rollout. `docs/spec-context.md` precludes automated runtime test suites for this kind of flow.
1057:

1060:## 11. System P&L page
1061:
1062:**Reference UI:** [prototypes/system-costs-page.html](prototypes/system-costs-page.html) — the committed high-fidelity mockup is the authoritative visual and interaction specification. Every production component in this section matches that mockup's structure, column order, status-row treatment, and interaction patterns.
1063:
1064:### 11.1 Route + permissions
1065:
1066:**Route:** `/system/llm-pnl` (client-side)
1067:**API base:** `/api/admin/llm-pnl/*`
1068:
1069:**Permissions:**
1070:- Gated by `requireSystemAdmin` middleware at [server/routes/llmUsage.ts](server/routes/llmUsage.ts) pattern.
1071:- Cross-org by design — this is the *one* admin surface that intentionally reads across every organisation.
1072:- No new permission key (`system_usage_view`) introduced; reuses the existing `requireSystemAdmin` check from the system routes suite.
1073:
1074:**Client-side route registration** in [client/src/App.tsx](client/src/App.tsx) — add under the existing `/system/*` route group. Lazy-loaded like every other system page per `architecture.md` client-side conventions.
1075:
1076:### 11.2 Service layer
1077:
1078:**File:** `server/services/systemPnlService.ts` (new)
1079:
1080:Methods:
1081:
1082:```ts
1083:export const systemPnlService = {
1084:  /** KPIs for a given period. */
1085:  getPnlSummary(period: { from: Date; to: Date }): Promise<PnlSummary>,
1086:
1087:  /** Grouping: by organisation. Returns up to N rows sorted by cost desc, plus a synthetic
1088:   *  aggregated overhead row (sum of system + analyzer cost across all orgs). */
1089:  getByOrganisation(period, limit?: number, filters?: OrgFilters): Promise<{ orgs: OrgRow[]; overhead: OverheadRow }>,
1090:
1091:  /** Grouping: by subaccount. Flat list across all orgs. */
1092:  getBySubaccount(period, limit?: number, filters?: SubacctFilters): Promise<SubacctRow[]>,
1093:
1094:  /** Grouping: by sourceType. 5 rows (agent_run / process_execution / iee / system / analyzer). */
1095:  getBySourceType(period): Promise<SourceTypeRow[]>,
1096:
1097:  /** Grouping: by provider + model. */
1098:  getByProviderModel(period): Promise<ProviderModelRow[]>,
1099:
1100:  /** 30-day daily trend (revenue + cost + profit + system overhead). */
1101:  getDailyTrend(days: number): Promise<DailyTrendRow[]>,
1102:
1103:  /** Top N individual calls by cost in the period (ORDER BY cost_raw DESC). Includes
1104:   *  non-billable rows (sourceType ∈ {'system','analyzer'}) whose revenue is null —
1105:   *  the list is a platform-overhead debugging surface, not a revenue leaderboard. */
1106:  getTopCalls(period, limit: number): Promise<TopCallRow[]>,
1107:
1108:  /** Full detail for one llm_requests row. */
1109:  getCallDetail(id: string): Promise<CallDetail>,
1110:};
1111:```
1112:
1113:**Data source per method:** `cost_aggregates` only carries scalar `totalCost*`, `totalTokens*`, `requestCount`, `errorCount` keyed by `(entityType, entityId, periodType, periodKey)`. Several P&L methods need data the aggregate table does not carry — avg latency, provider+model composite keys, distinct-org counts per `sourceType`, and per-row sparklines. The split is therefore:
1114:
1115:| Method | Primary source | Why |
1116:|---|---|---|
1117:| `getPnlSummary` | `cost_aggregates` (period + platform totals) | KPI numbers are scalar sums already denormalised |
1118:| `getByOrganisation` | `cost_aggregates` for the scalar columns + per-org sparkline values read from 30 daily rows; `subaccountCount` JOINed from `subaccounts` table | Aggregate carries the money math; subaccount count is a cheap JOIN; sparkline is 30 daily aggregate reads per org |
1119:| `getBySubaccount` | `cost_aggregates` (entity_type='subaccount') + `subaccounts` for org-name JOIN | Same pattern as org tab |
1120:| `getBySourceType` | `cost_aggregates` (entity_type='source_type') **plus** `llm_requests` for distinct-org and subaccount counts | Aggregate doesn't carry distinct-org counts per source_type; cheap enough to aggregate live from `llm_requests` because source_type cardinality is tiny |
1121:| `getByProviderModel` | `llm_requests` live — GROUP BY `(provider, model)` with AVG(providerLatencyMs) | Aggregate has no `provider+model` composite key nor any latency column. For the 30-day window this is a bounded scan (indexed by `provider, model, billingMonth`). If the query cost becomes load-bearing later, extend `cost_aggregates` with a `provider_model` entity_type + an `avg_latency_ms` column — deferred for now. |
1122:| `getDailyTrend` | `cost_aggregates` (entity_type='platform', periodType='daily') | Platform daily totals are already denormalised |
1123:| `getTopCalls` | `llm_requests` directly | Per-row granularity, `cost_aggregates` cannot answer. `ORDER BY cost_raw DESC` — see docstring above for why ranking is by cost, not revenue. |
1124:| `getCallDetail` | `llm_requests` (+ `llm_requests_archive` UNION post-P5) directly | Per-row granularity |
1125:
1126:**Caching:** no application-layer cache. `cost_aggregates` is pre-aggregated and sub-100ms under the composite index; the `llm_requests` live reads are bounded by indexed scans on `(organisation_id, billing_month)` / `(provider, model, billing_month)` and are sub-500ms at expected volumes. Revisit caching in a follow-up only if latency becomes visible.
1127:
1128:**Principal context:** admin reads bypass RLS via the existing `withAdminConnection` primitive at [server/lib/adminDbConnection.ts](server/lib/adminDbConnection.ts). This is a deliberate cross-tenant read, authorised by `requireSystemAdmin`.
1129:
1130:### 11.3 API endpoints
1131:
1132:All routes live in `server/routes/systemPnl.ts` (new), mounted under `/api/admin/llm-pnl/*`.
1133:
1134:**Response envelope:** every endpoint returns the `{data, meta}` wrapper defined in §19.9. The "Returns" column below names the TypeScript type of the `data` payload only — `meta` is uniform across every route (`period`, `generatedAt`, `ledgerRowsScanned`).
1135:
1136:| Method | Path | `data` payload type | Purpose |
1137:|---|---|---|---|
1138:| GET | `/summary?month=YYYY-MM` | `PnlSummary` | 4 KPI cards data |
1139:| GET | `/by-organisation?month=YYYY-MM&limit=N` | `{ orgs: OrgRow[]; overhead: OverheadRow }` | Tab 1 |
1140:| GET | `/by-subaccount?month=YYYY-MM&limit=N` | `SubacctRow[]` | Tab 2 |
1141:| GET | `/by-source-type?month=YYYY-MM` | `SourceTypeRow[]` | Tab 3 |
1142:| GET | `/by-provider-model?month=YYYY-MM` | `ProviderModelRow[]` | Tab 4 |
1143:| GET | `/trend?days=30` | `DailyTrendRow[]` | Chart |
1144:| GET | `/top-calls?month=YYYY-MM&limit=10` | `TopCallRow[]` | "Top calls by cost" list (bottom-of-page) |
1145:| GET | `/call/:id` | `CallDetail` | Detail drawer |
1146:
1147:Every route: `requireSystemAdmin` → service method → JSON response. `asyncHandler` wraps each handler per architecture convention.

1149:### 11.4 Page components
1150:
1151:**File tree:**

1154:client/src/pages/SystemPnlPage.tsx

1170:Page layout matches the mockup:
1171:

1173:2. 4 KPI cards in a 4-col grid (`.kpi-grid`)
1174:3. Grouping tabs (segmented control)
1175:4. Active table view (one of four)
1176:5. Trend chart
1177:6. Top calls list

1179:**Data fetching:** React Query (`useQuery`) per endpoint. Keys are `['systemPnl', tab, month]` / `['systemPnl', 'trend', days]` etc. `staleTime: 60_000` and `refetchInterval: 60_000` — the page auto-refetches every 60 seconds, matching the mockup's "updated every 60 seconds" footer claim verbatim.
1180:

1182:- Active tab: local state (`useState`).
1183:- Period: local state, defaults to current month.
1184:- Filters per column: local state, cleared by the "Clear all" button.
1185:
1186:No global store needed; this is a leaf page.

1188:### 11.4.1 Controls implemented in P4
1189:
1190:The mockup shows several controls the operator can interact with. Each is either specified here with a concrete P4 implementation, or explicitly marked **decorative** so no implementation work is required.
1191:
1192:| Control | Mockup location | P4 behaviour |
1193:|---|---|---|
1194:| **Auto-refresh ("updated every 60 seconds")** | Footer copy on line 1141 of the mockup | **Real.** React Query uses `refetchInterval: 60_000` across all `/api/admin/llm-pnl/*` queries. Footer copy is accurate. |
1195:| **Refresh button** | Top-right of page header (mockup line 137) | **Real.** Manual `queryClient.invalidateQueries(['systemPnl'])` — forces immediate refetch of all P&L queries. |
1196:| **Export CSV button** | Top-right of page header (mockup line 156) | **Real, client-side only.** Clicking the button serialises the currently-visible tab's React Query cache to CSV and triggers a browser download. No new API endpoint. Implementation is a ~30-line client-side helper (`exportTabAsCsv(tab, rows)`); columns match the rendered table verbatim. Scope: the active tab's rows at the current filter/sort. |
1197:| **View all (in "Top calls by cost" header)** | Mockup line 994 | **Real, as an anchor scroll + limit bump.** Clicking sets the client-side `topCallsLimit` state from 10 to 50 and smooth-scrolls to the top of the Top-calls section. No new page, no new route. "All" means "up to 50 in the current period," not "every row ever." |
1198:| **Footer link — "Margin policies"** | Mockup line 1144 | **Decorative.** Rendered as a `<span>` styled like a link but with no `href` and no click handler. Real destination deferred — see §17. |
1199:| **Footer link — "Retention"** | Mockup line 1145 | **Decorative.** Same treatment as "Margin policies." Real destination deferred — see §17. |
1200:| **Footer link — "Billing rules"** | Mockup line 1146 | **Decorative.** Same treatment as "Margin policies." Real destination deferred — see §17. |
1201:
1202:Rationale: the mockup makes visible commitments to the operator. Refresh, Export CSV, View all, and the 60s auto-refresh are cheap to honour with client-side-only work and the mockup would feel broken without them. Admin-only footer destinations (`Margin policies`, `Retention`, `Billing rules`) would balloon P4 scope into a multi-page admin suite — decorative-for-now is the cheapest honouring of the mockup's visual intent without committing P4 to pages that don't yet exist.
1203:
1204:### 11.5 Column contracts per tab
1205:
1206:See §19 Contracts for the full TypeScript types. Column order matches the mockup verbatim. Sort directions default to cost-descending. Filter UI on every column header follows the `ColHeader` dropdown pattern.
1207:
1208:| Tab | Columns | Sort default |
1209:|---|---|---|
1210:| By Organisation | Organisation \| Subaccounts \| Requests \| Revenue \| Cost \| Profit \| Margin \| % of Revenue \| Trend | Cost desc |
1211:| By Subaccount | Subaccount \| Organisation \| Requests \| Revenue \| Cost \| Profit \| Margin \| % of Revenue | Cost desc |
1212:| By Source Type | Source Type \| Orgs \| Requests \| Revenue \| Cost \| Profit \| Margin \| % of Cost | Cost desc |
1213:| By Provider / Model | Provider \| Model \| Requests \| Revenue \| Cost \| Profit \| Margin \| Avg Latency \| Share of Cost | Cost desc |
1214:
1215:**Overhead row treatment (applied wherever an overhead row renders):**
1216:- Revenue: em-dash
1217:- Profit: negative cost, displayed in muted slate-500 with a minus sign
1218:- Margin: "overhead" badge instead of percentage
1219:- Pulled out visually with a subtle indigo background
1220:
1221:**Which tabs render overhead rows** (matches `prototypes/system-costs-page.html`):
1222:
1223:| Tab | Overhead treatment |
1224:|---|---|
1225:| By Organisation | One synthetic aggregated overhead row (labelled `Overhead · Platform background work`) that sums `system` + `analyzer` cost across every org. The By Subaccount tab slices by a different dimension; see below. |
1226:| By Subaccount | No overhead row. Subaccount grouping has no natural home for platform-wide overhead (overhead has no subaccount), so the tab renders only subaccount rows. Aggregate overhead is visible via the Platform overhead KPI card and the `By Source Type` and `By Organisation` tabs. |
1227:| By Source Type | Two overhead rows — `system` and `analyzer` — rendered as separate rows per §19.5. |
1228:| By Provider / Model | No overhead row. Platform overhead crosses provider/model lines; splitting it by provider would add noise without observability win. Aggregate overhead is visible elsewhere. |
1229:
1230:On `By Source Type`, both `system` and `analyzer` render as overhead rows per the treatment above. The schema-level split between `system` and `analyzer` (added in §6.1) is preserved here so operators can see analyzer spend at a glance instead of hiding it behind a single "System" line.
1231:
1232:**Totals row at the bottom of each table:**
1233:- Rev/Cost/Profit: summed across all visible rows including every overhead row rendered on that tab
1234:- Margin: computed as net margin (profit/revenue) or noted as "net" if including overhead rows
1235:
1236:### 11.6 Detail drawer
1237:
1238:**Opens on:** clicking any row in "Top calls by cost."
1239:
1240:**Fields shown:**
1241:- Provider request ID (copyable)
1242:- Idempotency key
1243:- Full error message + code (if non-success)
1244:- Token breakdown (input, output, cached prompt tokens)
1245:- Latency breakdown (router overhead + provider latency)
1246:- Fallback chain (JSON-decoded from the column)
1247:- Retry attempt number
1248:- `parseFailureRawExcerpt` rendered in a monospace block if non-null
1249:- Links back to: originating run (if `runId` present), job (if `sourceId` present), organisation, subaccount
1250:- "Copy as support ticket" button — formats provider_request_id + model + error into a block suitable for pasting into an Anthropic support ticket

 exited 1 in 427ms:
1251:
1252:**Scope note:** rich-state interactions on the drawer (filter-by-request-ID inline, keyboard nav) are **deferred** — see §17. Base drawer ships with Phase 4.
1253:
1254:### 11.7 What the page does NOT do (scope discipline)
1255:
1256:- Not a billing dashboard — no invoice generation, no payment reconciliation.
1257:- Not a forecasting tool — no "projected monthly cost" figures.
1258:- Not a per-user drill-down — user-level cost views live on the existing Usage page.
1259:- Not an anomaly alert surface — "Platform overhead >15% of revenue for 3 days" alerting is deferred (§17).
1260:- Not a replacement for the existing Usage page — that page remains the subaccount-scoped view for org admins. The P&L page is platform-admin-only.

1263:
1264:## 12. Retention policy for `llm_requests`
1265:
1266:### 12.1 Problem
1267:
1268:`llm_requests` grows unbounded by design — it's a financial audit ledger. At steady-state with live clients, conservative estimate is 50,000–200,000 rows per month per paying org. With 10 paying orgs, that's ~2M rows/month, ~24M rows/year. Each row is ~1 KB (mostly hashes + numeric), so ~24 GB/year. Manageable but not trivial, and the indexes on this table multiply storage.
1269:
1270:**The purpose of retention is NOT cost reduction.** It is:
1271:- Faster queries on the hot path (last 90 days is what dashboards actually read).
1272:- Cleaner index rebuilds (smaller indexes rebuild faster on migration).
1273:- Operational safety: a single runaway analyzer run can't DoS the ledger.
1274:
1275:### 12.2 Decision
1276:
1277:**Keep full detail rows in `llm_requests` for `env.LLM_LEDGER_RETENTION_MONTHS` months (default 12).** After that, move rows to `llm_requests_archive` (same shape, subset of indexes).
1278:
1279:**`cost_aggregates` rollups are kept forever.** Daily rollups are tiny (one row per org per day per dimension — thousands of rows total, not millions) and power the long-term financial reports.
1280:
1281:### 12.3 `llm_requests_archive` (migration 0183)
1282:
1283:Shape: identical to `llm_requests` at migration time. Drizzle schema: share a common type shape, two Drizzle tables.
1284:
1285:Indexes: only the ones needed for occasional lookup by support/compliance:
1286:
1287:- `idempotency_key` — for proof-of-billing queries.
1288:- `provider_request_id` — for Anthropic support tickets.
1289:- `organisation_id, billing_month` — for "show me all calls for this org in 2026" support flows.
1290:
1291:**Not copied to archive:** partial indexes on `status`, `execution_phase`, `execution_id`, `feature_tag`. These are dashboard-hot; archived data doesn't need them.
1292:
1293:### 12.4 `llm-ledger-archive` job (new pg-boss job)
1294:
1295:**Files:**
1296:- `server/jobs/llmLedgerArchiveJob.ts` (new) — the job orchestration + DB transaction loop (impure).
1297:- `server/jobs/llmLedgerArchiveJobPure.ts` (new) — pure helpers extracted out of the job for testability. Exports `computeArchiveCutoff(retentionMonths, now)`.
1298:
1299:**Schedule:** nightly at 03:00 UTC (pg-boss cron).
1300:
1301:**Pure helper (`llmLedgerArchiveJobPure.ts`):**
1302:
1303:```ts
1304:/**
1305: * Cutoff for archive-eligibility: rows strictly older than `retentionMonths`
1306: * calendar months before `now` are moved to the archive table.
1307: *
1308: * `now` is injected for test determinism; the caller passes `new Date()` at
1309: * runtime. Uses `setMonth(getMonth() - n)` rather than day arithmetic so the
1310: * cutoff tracks month boundaries rather than a naive 30-day window.
1311: */
1312:export function computeArchiveCutoff(retentionMonths: number, now: Date): Date {
1313:  const cutoff = new Date(now.getTime());
1314:  cutoff.setMonth(cutoff.getMonth() - retentionMonths);
1315:  return cutoff;
1316:}
1317:```
1318:
1319:The corresponding test at `server/jobs/__tests__/ledgerArchivePure.test.ts` (§14.8a) exercises this helper directly — no DB, no mocks.
1320:
1321:**Shape (`llmLedgerArchiveJob.ts`):**
1322:
1323:```ts
1324:export async function archiveOldLedgerRows(): Promise<ArchiveResult> {
1325:  const cutoff = computeArchiveCutoff(env.LLM_LEDGER_RETENTION_MONTHS, new Date());
1326:
1327:  // Move rows in 10k-row chunks to bound transaction size.
1328:  // Postgres does NOT support `DELETE ... ORDER BY ... LIMIT` directly, so we
1329:  // pick ids with a separate SELECT first (cheap because `created_at` is indexed),
1330:  // then copy + delete those specific ids. Using `FOR UPDATE SKIP LOCKED`
1331:  // keeps the job safe under concurrent runs (though the nightly cadence
1332:  // makes concurrency very unlikely).
1333:  let totalMoved = 0;
1334:  for (;;) {
1335:    const moved = await db.transaction(async (tx) => {
1336:      const result = await tx.execute(sql`
1337:        WITH doomed AS (
1338:          SELECT id
1339:          FROM llm_requests
1340:          WHERE created_at < ${cutoff}
1341:          ORDER BY created_at
1342:          LIMIT 10000
1343:          FOR UPDATE SKIP LOCKED
1344:        ),
1345:        inserted AS (
1346:          INSERT INTO llm_requests_archive
1347:          SELECT * FROM llm_requests
1348:          WHERE id IN (SELECT id FROM doomed)
1349:          RETURNING id
1350:        )
1351:        DELETE FROM llm_requests
1352:        WHERE id IN (SELECT id FROM inserted)
1353:        RETURNING 1;
1354:      `);
1355:      return result.rowCount ?? 0;
1356:    });
1357:    totalMoved += moved;
1358:    if (moved < 10000) break;
1359:  }
1360:  return { totalMoved, cutoff };
1361:}
1362:```
1363:
1364:**Safety:**
1365:
1366:- CTE with `DELETE ... RETURNING` + `INSERT` in a single transaction means a row is either in `llm_requests` OR in `llm_requests_archive`, never both, never neither.
1367:- `ORDER BY created_at LIMIT 10000` bounds each transaction to ~10 MB.
1368:- Job is idempotent — re-running it on the same day does nothing if the first run cleared the cutoff.
1369:
1370:**Verification:**
1371:
1372:- `getCallDetail(id)` reads from both tables (UNION ALL) transparently so detail drawer works for archived rows.
1373:- `getTopCalls()` reads only `llm_requests` (the last 30 days are never archived).
1374:
1375:### 12.5 Environment + config
1376:
1377:**New env var:** `LLM_LEDGER_RETENTION_MONTHS` (default: `12`). Declared in [server/lib/env.ts](server/lib/env.ts).
1378:
1379:No admin-facing config UI — this is an infrastructure tunable, not a business decision.
1380:
1381:### 12.6 Deferred from retention (see §17)
1382:
1383:- **`llm_requests_archive` further tiering** (e.g. "after 36 months, move to cold storage or dump to S3"). Not needed until data volume justifies it.
1384:- **Per-org retention overrides.** If a client demands 5-year audit retention by contract, that's a commercial conversation handled outside this spec.
1385:
1386:---
1387:
1388:## 13. Permissions & RLS
1389:
1390:### 13.1 `llm_requests` — existing RLS state
1391:
1392:`llm_requests` is already listed in [server/config/rlsProtectedTables.ts](server/config/rlsProtectedTables.ts) as an org-scoped table with RLS enabled. The new columns added in this spec (`source_id`, `feature_tag`, `parse_failure_raw_excerpt`, `abort_reason`) do not change the RLS policy — the `organisation_id` column remains the scoping axis, and all new columns are dependent on that column for access.
1393:
1394:**No RLS migration required** for the column additions. Verify after migration 0180 lands that `verify-rls-coverage.sh` still passes.
1395:
1396:### 13.2 `llm_requests_archive` — new table RLS requirement
1397:
1398:Per §4 of the spec-authoring checklist: every new tenant-scoped table must have (1) RLS policy, (2) manifest entry, (3) route guard, (4) principal-scoped context.
1399:
1400:**Application to `llm_requests_archive`:**
1401:
1402:1. **RLS policy:** identical to `llm_requests` — rows readable only when `organisation_id = current_setting('app.organisation_id')::uuid` OR when the caller is admin-connection-scoped (admin reads bypass).
1403:2. **Manifest entry:** add `llm_requests_archive` to `server/config/rlsProtectedTables.ts` in the same migration (0183) that creates the table. `verify-rls-coverage.sh` enforces this.
1404:3. **Route guard:** no HTTP route reads the archive directly. `getCallDetail()` reads via `systemPnlService` which runs under `requireSystemAdmin` + `withAdminConnection`. If an org-scoped route needs archived data later, that requires a separate spec.
1405:4. **Principal-scoped context:** admin reads use `withAdminConnection`. No agent-execution path reads the archive.
1406:
1407:### 13.3 System P&L page — admin-scoped reads
1408:
1409:**Deliberate cross-tenant read:** the System P&L page is the one UI that reads across all organisations by design. It is gated by:
1410:
1411:- `requireSystemAdmin` middleware on every `/api/admin/llm-pnl/*` route.
1412:- `withAdminConnection` for the actual DB queries (bypasses RLS).
1413:- No other route or UI exposes this data.
1414:
1415:**Why not a new permission key?** `requireSystemAdmin` already exists and is sufficient. Introducing `system_pnl_view` would be redundant — there is no sub-role of "system admin who can see skills but not costs" that we want to express today.
1416:
1417:### 13.4 `cost_aggregates` — already covered
1418:
1419:`cost_aggregates` is already in the RLS manifest. The new `entity_type = 'source_type' | 'feature_tag'` values don't change its row shape, just add writes. No migration to RLS policy.
1420:
1421:### 13.5 System-level rows and RLS
1422:
1423:Ledger rows with `sourceType = 'system'` or `'analyzer'` still have `organisation_id` set (the organisation that initiated the analyzer run). These rows ARE subject to RLS like every other row.
1424:
1425:The exception is system rows with no attributable org — e.g. a periodic platform-wide maintenance job that spans orgs. Today, no such caller exists. If one is added, we either assign it a synthetic "platform" org UUID OR add an `organisation_id` nullable column + RLS policy extension. Out of scope for this spec.

1024:Replace the existing `Promise.race([withBackoff(...), timeoutPromise])` pattern with the `AbortController` pattern — they do the same thing, but the latter actually kills the underlying fetch (see §2.3).
1025:
1026:**`withBackoff` retention:** `routeCall` internally uses its own retry strategy via the router's fallback-chain logic. The analyzer's current `maxAttempts: 3` for parse failures specifically is handled by the `postProcess` hook re-throwing `ParseFailureError`, which the router's retry policy classifies as retryable (same classification the analyzer uses today — 429, 503, 529, PARSE_FAILURE).

1037:
1038:Fourth migration. Same mechanical shape as §10.1–§10.3. Replace the direct `anthropicAdapter.call()` invocation at `server/services/skillAnalyzerService.ts:2063` with `llmRouter.routeCall()`.
1039:
1040:- `sourceType: 'analyzer'`.
1041:- `sourceId` — `skill_analyzer_jobs.id` of the enclosing analyzer job. Per the analyzer-row invariant in §6.3, `sourceType='analyzer'` means `llm_requests.source_id` joins cleanly to `skill_analyzer_jobs.id`; all four analyzer sites (three job-layer, one service-layer) must honour that invariant so the P&L page's drawer link-back to the job works deterministically. If the call site does not have a job id in scope today, thread one through from the job that invokes the service (every code path that reaches `skillAnalyzerService.ts:2063` is started by a `skillAnalyzerJob.ts` run, so the id is available upstream).
1042:- `featureTag` — pick a stable kebab-case tag that distinguishes this site from the three job-layer sites (e.g. `skill-analyzer-service-<operation>`, where `<operation>` reflects the specific call the service is making; the exact tag is chosen at implementation time once the site's context is in hand).
1043:- `systemCallerPolicy` — `'bypass_routing'` if the site pins a specific model today; otherwise `'respect_routing'`.
1044:- Thread the existing `AbortController` / `AbortSignal` through to `llmRouter.routeCall()` per §8.1.
1045:
1046:### 10.5 Verification
1047:
1048:After the four migrations, run the analyzer end-to-end on a test import and verify:
1049:
1050:1. `SELECT COUNT(*) FROM llm_requests WHERE feature_tag LIKE 'skill-analyzer-%' AND created_at > <before_test>` returns a non-zero count roughly equal to the number of candidates × number of LLM calls per candidate (summed across the three job-layer sites and the service-layer site from §10.4).
1051:2. Cross-check `providerRequestId` values against the Anthropic console — every row's provider_request_id should match an entry in Anthropic's log (within a tolerance for the specific request).
1052:3. `SELECT SUM(cost_with_margin) FROM llm_requests WHERE feature_tag LIKE 'skill-analyzer-%' AND billing_month = '2026-MM'` gives a non-zero total that appears in `cost_aggregates` rolled up under `entity_type = 'feature_tag'`.
1053:4. Let a classify timeout via its existing `SKILL_CLASSIFY_TIMEOUT_MS` path and verify the resulting ledger row carries `status = 'aborted_by_caller'` and `abort_reason = 'caller_timeout'`.
1054:5. Simulate a parse failure by temporarily breaking the schema validator and verify `parseFailureRawExcerpt` is populated ≤2 KB.
1055:
1056:Verification is manual during Phase 3 rollout. `docs/spec-context.md` precludes automated runtime test suites for this kind of flow.

1060:## 11. System P&L page
1061:
1062:**Reference UI:** [prototypes/system-costs-page.html](prototypes/system-costs-page.html) — the committed high-fidelity mockup is the authoritative visual and interaction specification. Every production component in this section matches that mockup's structure, column order, status-row treatment, and interaction patterns.
1063:
1064:### 11.1 Route + permissions
1065:
1066:**Route:** `/system/llm-pnl` (client-side)
1067:**API base:** `/api/admin/llm-pnl/*`
1068:
1069:**Permissions:**
1070:- Gated by `requireSystemAdmin` middleware at [server/routes/llmUsage.ts](server/routes/llmUsage.ts) pattern.
1071:- Cross-org by design — this is the *one* admin surface that intentionally reads across every organisation.
1072:- No new permission key (`system_usage_view`) introduced; reuses the existing `requireSystemAdmin` check from the system routes suite.
1073:
1074:**Client-side route registration** in [client/src/App.tsx](client/src/App.tsx) — add under the existing `/system/*` route group. Lazy-loaded like every other system page per `architecture.md` client-side conventions.
1075:
1076:### 11.2 Service layer
1077:
1078:**File:** `server/services/systemPnlService.ts` (new)
1079:
1080:Methods:
1081:
1082:```ts
1083:export const systemPnlService = {
1084:  /** KPIs for a given period. */
1085:  getPnlSummary(period: { from: Date; to: Date }): Promise<PnlSummary>,
1086:
1087:  /** Grouping: by organisation. Returns up to N rows sorted by cost desc, plus a synthetic
1088:   *  aggregated overhead row (sum of system + analyzer cost across all orgs). */
1089:  getByOrganisation(period, limit?: number, filters?: OrgFilters): Promise<{ orgs: OrgRow[]; overhead: OverheadRow }>,
1090:
1091:  /** Grouping: by subaccount. Flat list across all orgs. */
1092:  getBySubaccount(period, limit?: number, filters?: SubacctFilters): Promise<SubacctRow[]>,
1093:
1094:  /** Grouping: by sourceType. 5 rows (agent_run / process_execution / iee / system / analyzer). */
1095:  getBySourceType(period): Promise<SourceTypeRow[]>,
1096:
1097:  /** Grouping: by provider + model. */
1098:  getByProviderModel(period): Promise<ProviderModelRow[]>,
1099:
1100:  /** 30-day daily trend (revenue + cost + profit + system overhead). */
1101:  getDailyTrend(days: number): Promise<DailyTrendRow[]>,
1102:
1103:  /** Top N individual calls by cost in the period (ORDER BY cost_raw DESC). Includes
1104:   *  non-billable rows (sourceType ∈ {'system','analyzer'}) whose revenue is null —
1105:   *  the list is a platform-overhead debugging surface, not a revenue leaderboard. */
1106:  getTopCalls(period, limit: number): Promise<TopCallRow[]>,
1107:
1108:  /** Full detail for one llm_requests row. */
1109:  getCallDetail(id: string): Promise<CallDetail>,
1110:};
1111:```
1112:
1113:**Data source per method:** `cost_aggregates` only carries scalar `totalCost*`, `totalTokens*`, `requestCount`, `errorCount` keyed by `(entityType, entityId, periodType, periodKey)`. Several P&L methods need data the aggregate table does not carry — avg latency, provider+model composite keys, distinct-org counts per `sourceType`, and per-row sparklines. The split is therefore:
1114:
1115:| Method | Primary source | Why |
1116:|---|---|---|
1117:| `getPnlSummary` | `cost_aggregates` (period + platform totals) | KPI numbers are scalar sums already denormalised |
1118:| `getByOrganisation` | `cost_aggregates` for the scalar columns + per-org sparkline values read from 30 daily rows; `subaccountCount` JOINed from `subaccounts` table | Aggregate carries the money math; subaccount count is a cheap JOIN; sparkline is 30 daily aggregate reads per org |
1119:| `getBySubaccount` | `cost_aggregates` (entity_type='subaccount') + `subaccounts` for org-name JOIN | Same pattern as org tab |
1120:| `getBySourceType` | `cost_aggregates` (entity_type='source_type') **plus** `llm_requests` for distinct-org and subaccount counts | Aggregate doesn't carry distinct-org counts per source_type; cheap enough to aggregate live from `llm_requests` because source_type cardinality is tiny |
1121:| `getByProviderModel` | `llm_requests` live — GROUP BY `(provider, model)` with AVG(providerLatencyMs) | Aggregate has no `provider+model` composite key nor any latency column. For the 30-day window this is a bounded scan (indexed by `provider, model, billingMonth`). If the query cost becomes load-bearing later, extend `cost_aggregates` with a `provider_model` entity_type + an `avg_latency_ms` column — deferred for now. |
1122:| `getDailyTrend` | `cost_aggregates` (entity_type='platform', periodType='daily') | Platform daily totals are already denormalised |
1123:| `getTopCalls` | `llm_requests` directly | Per-row granularity, `cost_aggregates` cannot answer. `ORDER BY cost_raw DESC` — see docstring above for why ranking is by cost, not revenue. |
1124:| `getCallDetail` | `llm_requests` (+ `llm_requests_archive` UNION post-P5) directly | Per-row granularity |
1125:
1126:**Caching:** no application-layer cache. `cost_aggregates` is pre-aggregated and sub-100ms under the composite index; the `llm_requests` live reads are bounded by indexed scans on `(organisation_id, billing_month)` / `(provider, model, billing_month)` and are sub-500ms at expected volumes. Revisit caching in a follow-up only if latency becomes visible.
1127:
1128:**Principal context:** admin reads bypass RLS via the existing `withAdminConnection` primitive at [server/lib/adminDbConnection.ts](server/lib/adminDbConnection.ts). This is a deliberate cross-tenant read, authorised by `requireSystemAdmin`.
1129:
1130:### 11.3 API endpoints
1131:
1132:All routes live in `server/routes/systemPnl.ts` (new), mounted under `/api/admin/llm-pnl/*`.
1133:
1134:**Response envelope:** every endpoint returns the `{data, meta}` wrapper defined in §19.9. The "Returns" column below names the TypeScript type of the `data` payload only — `meta` is uniform across every route (`period`, `generatedAt`, `ledgerRowsScanned`).
1135:
1136:| Method | Path | `data` payload type | Purpose |
1137:|---|---|---|---|
1138:| GET | `/summary?month=YYYY-MM` | `PnlSummary` | 4 KPI cards data |
1139:| GET | `/by-organisation?month=YYYY-MM&limit=N` | `{ orgs: OrgRow[]; overhead: OverheadRow }` | Tab 1 |
1140:| GET | `/by-subaccount?month=YYYY-MM&limit=N` | `SubacctRow[]` | Tab 2 |
1141:| GET | `/by-source-type?month=YYYY-MM` | `SourceTypeRow[]` | Tab 3 |
1142:| GET | `/by-provider-model?month=YYYY-MM` | `ProviderModelRow[]` | Tab 4 |
1143:| GET | `/trend?days=30` | `DailyTrendRow[]` | Chart |

1145:| GET | `/call/:id` | `CallDetail` | Detail drawer |

1179:**Data fetching:** React Query (`useQuery`) per endpoint. Keys are `['systemPnl', tab, month]` / `['systemPnl', 'trend', days]` etc. `staleTime: 60_000` and `refetchInterval: 60_000` — the page auto-refetches every 60 seconds, matching the mockup's "updated every 60 seconds" footer claim verbatim.

1182:- Active tab: local state (`useState`).
1183:- Period: local state, defaults to current month.
1184:- Filters per column: local state, cleared by the "Clear all" button.
